# Changelog

All notable changes to GenomeInsight will be documented in this file.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/).

## [Unreleased]

### Fixed

- **LAI `lai_bundle v2.0.0` residual Middle-Eastern misclassification — re-balanced + republished (`fix-lai-mid-rebalance`):** After the European fix, the held-out per-superpopulation inference gate still showed **MID 2/5** (mean self-frac 0.384; the three misses all went to EUR at 0.40–0.50). Root cause: MID is continentally intermediate (between EUR/AFR/CSA) and the gnomix training panel was EUR-heavy (EUR 738 vs MID 152 founders), so the decision boundary pulled borderline MID windows into EUR — a milder instance of the same imbalance class as the EUR=3 bug, and one the mean per-window accuracy (06e) is blind to. Fixed by class-balancing the reference panel with `--per-region-cap=250` (`scripts/lai_bundle_v2/env.sh::PER_REGION_CAP`, now the default → wired through `04c_filter_single_ancestry.py`): the panel goes 985/810/762/743/238/157/30 → **250/250/250/250/238/157/30**, ~tripling MID's relative weight; the held-out split holds 5/superpop out of training (HG01502 stays a non-founder). Retrained all 22 chromosomes on the re-balanced panel and re-validated against the held-out per-superpopulation gate: **MID 2/5 → 5/5** (mean self-frac 0.384 → 0.671) with **no regression** (AFR/AMR/CSA/EAS/EUR/OCE all 5/5; held-out Iberian HG01502 still classifies 0.95 EUR). New tarball **sha256 `36abb5f2ed95011aff1227c894f52597ef5c31adb5a132fafdf0830eabf14bff`, 1,723,731,810 B** (build_date 2026-06-05), republished (`--clobber`) to the already-public `lai-bundle-v2.0.0` release with all five sha/size pins bumped (`bundles/manifest.json`, `backend/db/database_registry.py`, `tests/backend/test_manifest.py`, `test_lai_bundle_registry.py`, `test_database_registry_lai.py`) + the `test_lai.py` HG01502 drift-monitor reference recalibrated, and `bundle-release.yml` verify green. Mean per-window accuracy 0.865 (was ~0.90) is an accepted balance trade-off — capping costs the large classes some training data, but the held-out per-superpopulation inference gate (not the per-window mean) is the publication arbiter, and every superpopulation still classifies correctly. Also fixed **phase-05 BUG F**: gnomix ran a post-train inference on its full 4091-sample query and hung for hours (`Phasing individual N/4091`); `05_train_gnomix.sh` now hands gnomix a 2-sample query (the trained model is query-independent — training reads `reference_file` + `sample_map` + the seeded simulation only), so the SLURM array completes on its own and the `afterok` finish fires cleanly with no harvest babysitting.

- **LAI `lai_bundle v2.0.0` European misclassification — rebuilt + republished (release-blocking; #302, closes #300):** The published v2.0.0 LAI bundle classified Europeans as non-European — a held-out 1000G Iberian (HG01502/IBS) run through `run_lai_analysis` came back **94% CSA / 0.3% EUR**. Root cause: phase-04's `scripts/lai_bundle_v2/04c_filter_single_ancestry.py` selected the gnomix training panel by `max_q >= 0.95` (≥95% one fastmixture/ADMIXTURE component), but continentally-intermediate ancestries (EUR/MID/AMR) never form a clean single component at any K, so the cutoff dropped **767/770 EUR** (and all MID), leaving **EUR=3** in training; a model trained on 3 Europeans assigned every European to the nearest well-trained class (CSA). The bundle's 0.97 mean per-window accuracy was blind to it (no EUR in train/val, and the re-export self-check is "approximate, not a correctness proof"). Fixed by #299 (select the reference panel by the curated gnomAD `genetic_region` superpopulation labels + a light `--min-q` admixture-outlier floor + a build-time per-region composition gate `--min-per-region`, replacing the `max_q` cutoff) and rebuilt end-to-end on the cluster: panel **EUR 3→743, MID 0→157, AMR 85→238** (7 ancestries incl. MID — the broken bundle was 6, no MID), gnomix retrained over all 22 chromosomes (honest ~0.90 mean per-window accuracy), new tarball **sha256 `f2d8b0a2c1b9249c3f7b3b69a3ec4426d20860fa659fc63993c33f61f8d1c791`, 1,725,028,142 B**, republished (`--clobber`) to the already-public `lai-bundle-v2.0.0` release with `bundles/manifest.json` + `backend/db/database_registry.py` `DATABASES["lai_bundle"]` bumped (build_date 2026-06-04) and `bundle-release.yml` verify green. **New gold-standard gate — held-out per-superpopulation inference accuracy** (`scripts/lai_bundle_v2/06f_select_heldout.py` → `extract_heldout_fixtures.py` → `06f_heldout_superpop_accuracy.py`): hold N samples per superpopulation OUT of gnomix training, run each through the production inference path against the assembled bundle, assert each classifies to its own superpopulation — this catches the per-population misclassification the mean per-window accuracy (`06e`) is blind to. Result on the rebuilt bundle: **EUR 5/5 (0.985), AMR 5/5, AFR/CSA/EAS/OCE 5/5 — 32/35; MID 2/5** (a known residual — MID is continentally intermediate and adjacent to the much-larger EUR, so the boundary favours EUR; follow-up: rebuild with `--per-region-cap` and/or more MID training samples). Also fixed two phase-05 build-script defects surfaced by the rebuild: the per-chromosome SLURM-array tasks raced copying `sample_map.txt` to one shared `$GNOMIX_DIR` path (NFS `EEXIST` → `set -e` task death → requeue/re-train loop) — now passed read-only from `$ADMIX_DIR`, with `--no-requeue` + `--mem=64G` baked into `slurm/05_train_gnomix.sbatch`; and documented the gnomix post-train inference-on-the-full-panel hang + the model-harvest workaround (`05_train_gnomix.sh`). The Step-36 nightly `TestRealBundleLAIAccuracy` was re-pointed from the too-sparse `synthetic_eur_ancestrydna.txt` (~5k SNPs = 0.3% of the LAI panel → a degenerate call on *any* bundle) to a dense held-out `tests/fixtures/heldout_eur_HG01502.adna.txt.gz` (~666k sites, public 1000G → committable) with a robust property gate (top population == EUR and EUR ≥ 0.85); the nightly slow-tier is green.

### Added

- **AncestryDNA Integration + Multi-Source Sample Merging — Phases 0–3 ship (Step 89 / Plan §18.3, §2.4):** Rollup of the four-phase initiative tracked in `docs/AncestryDNA_Integration_Plan.md` + `docs/AncestryDNA_Implementation_Steps.md`. Closes PRD §15 P0 (`AncestryDNA raw data support`); promoted from "Post-v1 Roadmap" to a new "Shipped in v1.x" subsection in `prd.md` §15.
  - **Phase 0 — Foundations (Steps 1–25a).** Rebuilt VEP `vep_bundle v2.0.0` (~840k union 23andMe v5 ∪ AncestryDNA v2.0 rsids) and LAI `lai_bundle v2.0.0` as GitHub Release assets with manifest semver as the authoritative version field; bundle release runbooks + `workflow_dispatch` workflow (`scripts/build_vep_bundle.py --bundle-version`, `scripts/lai_bundle_v2/run_rebuild.sh`, `docs/bundle-release-runbook.md`, `docs/lai-bundle-release-runbook.md`, `.github/workflows/bundle-release.yml`). HTTP 409 `bundle_version_too_old` gate on AncestryDNA uploads with pre-v2.0.0 bundles (`backend/api/routes/ingest.py`). Per-sample `annotation_state(key PK, value, updated_at)` kv table for bundle-version provenance (Plan §7.1). `backend/services/staleness.py::is_sample_stale` + `backend/api/dependencies.py::require_fresh_sample` 423 gate applied to every sample-scoped analysis route (Plan §7.5), locked by a drift-guard test that parameterizes over the gated + opt-out route lists. `<StaleSampleGate>` frontend banner. Soft LAI staleness gate (`degraded_coverage: true` on AncestryDNA, never 423). Backup/restore bundle-version gate (`backend/api/routes/backup.py`, `RestoreStep.tsx`). Alembic migration `008_annotation_state_backfill.py` (idempotent per-sample-DB walk, `INSERT OR IGNORE vep_bundle_version='v1.0.0'`). App version bumped `0.1.0 → 0.2.0`; `packaging` added as a direct dependency. AncestryDNA upload disk-space pre-check + bundle-update affordance in the setup wizard.
  - **Phase 1 — AncestryDNA Single-Sample Ingestion (Steps 26–45).** Shared parser layer (`backend/ingestion/{base,chromosomes,dispatcher,parser_ancestrydna}.py`) with `SourceVendor` enum, `ParsedVariant` / `ParseResult` dataclasses, `detect_vendor()` + `parse()` head-line dispatch, per-vendor chromosome maps (`25→X` for AncestryDNA PAR, `26→MT`). AncestryDNA v2.0 parser handles `00`/`A0` no-calls, hemizygous X/Y, PAR collapse, indels (`I`/`D`, both orderings), mixed-case alleles, CRLF, `utf-8 errors="replace"`, legacy `kgp*` IDs passthrough; element-wise no-call rule + uppercase-and-sort allele canonicalization. 23andMe parser refactored onto shared base (`ParseResult.version` migrated `FormatVersion → str`). Ingest route emits `file_format = f"{vendor.value}_{version}"` (`ancestrydna_v2.0` / `23andme_v5`). Setup wizard accepts AncestryDNA; the "planned for a future release" rejection branch removed. Curated `tests/fixtures/sample_ancestrydna_v2.txt` (500–1000 hand-synthesized rsIDs covering autosomes, chrX/Y, PAR, MT, no-calls, indels, `kgp*`, APOE, MTHFR) + `*_malformed.txt` / `*_crlf.txt` / `*_non_utf8_byte.txt` fixtures. Regenerated mini VEP bundle (`tests/fixtures/mini_vep_bundle.db`) for AncestryDNA rsID coverage. Synthetic full-size EUR fixture (`scripts/regenerate_fixtures.py --vendor=ancestrydna`). Slow-tier nightly real-bundle annotation regression test + `.github/workflows/nightly.yml`. Setup-wizard Playwright E2E (happy-path + 409 gate banner). `frontend/src/test/setup-{upload,wizard}-step.test.tsx` AncestryDNA coverage.
  - **Phase 2 — Individual Aggregation Model (Steps 46–59).** Alembic migration `009_add_individuals_table.py` — `individuals(id, display_name, notes, biological_sex, created_at, updated_at)` reference-DB table + nullable `samples.individual_id` FK with `ON DELETE SET NULL`. Seven `/api/individuals` routes (list, create, detail, patch, delete, link-sample, unlink-sample) with 409 on double-link, 404 on nonexistent, dedup of aggregated findings across linked samples. React Query hooks (`frontend/src/api/individuals.ts`). Two-level sample selector in `TopNav` (individuals expand → samples; "Unassigned" group for `individual_id IS NULL`). `/individuals/{id}` detail page with aggregated high-confidence findings + multi-source provenance chips. Settings → Samples "Assign to individual" dropdown. Sex-thresholds validation script (`scripts/validate_sex_thresholds.py`) + bio-validator-signed threshold attestation (`docs/sex_inference_threshold_validation.md`). New `backend/services/sex_inference.py` with `_PAR1` / `_PAR2` boundaries + `_THRESHOLD_XY_CONFIRM` / `_THRESHOLD_PAR_NOISE` constants; `assign_haplogroups` rewired off the deleted `_infer_sex_from_variants`. Backfill script for candidate same-individual pairs (`scripts/backfill_individuals.py`, suggestions-only — never auto-executes). E2E linking flow + Phase 2 frontend coverage gate.
  - **Phase 3 — Genotype Merging (Steps 60–88).** Shared `backend/analysis/zygosity.py::is_no_call` adopted across 13 raw-genotype modules (`traits.py`, `gene_health.py`, `sleep.py`, `nutrigenomics.py`, `fitness.py`, `methylation.py`, `skin.py`, `allergy.py`, `pharmacogenomics.py`, `prs.py`, `apoe.py`, `ancestry.py`, `lai_runner.py`) — byte-identical-output parity test over the matrix. `_classify_genotype` reclassifies `"00"` + indel codes (`DD`/`II`/`DI`/`ID`) as `nocall` with bio-validator sign-off on QC-stats denominators. Per-sample schema **v7 → v8** bump (`SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION = 8`): `raw_variants` gains `source` / `concordance` / `discordant_alt_genotype` / `alt_rsid` text columns; merged-sample DBs use `(chrom, pos)` PK on `raw_variants` while unmerged keep `rsid` PK (`is_merged_sample` factory parameter); new single-row `merge_provenance(id=1, ...)` table. `backend/services/sample_merge.py` orchestrator — stale-source 423 block, individual-membership validation, status=complete check, coordinate-indexed in-memory merge with VEP-bundle canonical-rsid lookup, three strategies (`flag_only` default + `prefer_higher_quality` / `prefer_newer`), deterministic `file_hash = SHA-256(S1.file_hash ‖ S2.file_hash ‖ strategy ‖ str(SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION))`, batched writes, `merge_provenance` row, async Huey annotation enqueue. `backend/services/sample_delete.py` source-deletion cascade (merged children deleted before sources). Merge preview dry-run route (`POST /api/individuals/{id}/merge/preview`), commit route (`POST /api/individuals/{id}/merge`), `GET /api/samples/{id}/merge-provenance`, paginated `GET /api/samples/{id}/concordance-report?limit&offset` (default 50, max 500). Frontend: `MergeWizard` 3-step modal (strategy → preview → SSE-bound commit), `/samples/{id}/concordance` page with summary card + paginated discordant-loci table, variant table `Source` (S₁/S₂/both) + `Concordance` (match/filled-nocall/discordant/unique) filter chips, post-merge re-watch modal driven by `GET /api/samples/{merged_id}/watched-variants/migrate-from-sources` + SSE annotation-channel gating. Merge E2E (`tests/e2e/merge-samples.spec.ts`) + Phase 3 frontend coverage gate (≥70%) + slow-tier merge performance guard (700k×2 → <30 s WSL2 reference). End-user `docs/multi-source-merging.md` walkthrough cross-linked from `docs/usage-guide.md`.

### Changed

- **PRD §15 — Post-v1 Roadmap reshuffle (Step 89; Plan §18.3):** AncestryDNA P0 row moved out of the Post-v1 Roadmap table into a new "Shipped in v1.x" subsection above it, listing v0.2.0 as the shipping app version and v2.0.0 as the catalog-version line for both the VEP and LAI bundles. The Post-v1 Roadmap table now starts at P1 (MyHeritage / Nebula).

- **Multi-source merging end-user doc (Step 88 / MRG-11; Plan §15.1, §10):** New `docs/multi-source-merging.md` — end-to-end walkthrough for the Phase 3 merge flow: uploading both raw files, creating an individual, linking both samples, running the merge wizard (strategy choice + concordance preview + confirm), reading the merged dashboard's added `Source` / `Concordance` variant-table columns (Step 71), opening the concordance report page (Step 70's summary card + paginated discordant-loci table), and migrating watched variants via the post-merge re-watch modal (Step 72). The doc translates the data-model contract from Plan §10 into user-facing language: the merged sample as an independent `samples` row (`file_format="merged_v1"`), the three strategies (`flag_only` default + the two `prefer_*` variants), the `??` canonical no-call sentinel for `flag_only`-withheld calls (Plan §10.3 / `backend/analysis/zygosity.py::is_no_call`), the per-locus concordance buckets (`match` / `filled_nocall` / `discordant` / `unique_S1` / `unique_S2` / `collapsed_rsid`), tags/watches non-propagation across the merge (Plan §10.4 invariant — `variant_tags` and `watched_variants` keep `rsid` as PK and are not transferred to the new sample DB, locked by Step 79's `test_tag_watch_non_propagation.py`), the source-deletion cascade (Plan §10.8 / Step 66 / `backend/services/sample_delete.py`, locked by Step 82's `test_sample_delete_cascade.py`), the deterministic `file_hash` derivation (`SHA-256(S1.file_hash ‖ S2.file_hash ‖ strategy ‖ str(SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION))`, locked by Step 77's `test_sample_merge.py::test_remerge_hash_invariants` re-merge contract), and the stale-source HTTP 423 block (Plan §7.5 / `backend/api/dependencies.py::require_fresh_sample`, locked by Step 80). Cross-links into Plan §9 (Individuals) and Plan §10 (Sample Merging) for technical-contract depth; cross-link added from `docs/usage-guide.md` FAQ ("Can I analyze multiple samples?" — the natural single anchor in the existing single-sample-only guide). Docs-only step; no production code touched, no tests added — the surfaces the doc describes are all already shipped and covered by Steps 46–87. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 tiered-test policy this is not in the cross-cutting / Alembic-migration / sample-schema-declaration / phase-boundary lists, so no test sweep was required; ran `ls docs/multi-source-merging.md` to confirm the file exists. The doc closes out the MRG-11 deliverable from `docs/AncestryDNA_Implementation_Steps.md` Step 88 ("user walkthrough — uploading two raw files, linking under an individual, merging, reading the concordance report, post-merge re-watch") with one follow-up step in the AncestryDNA initiative (Step 89 / final cleanup + CHANGELOG + PRD-roadmap move) outstanding.
- **Phase 3 frontend coverage gate (Step 87 / MRG-12; Plan §15.1, §2.4):** Phase-boundary sweep step verifying the four Phase 3 frontend test files land green and clear the ≥70% coverage floor (CLAUDE.md SOP #8 "Definition of Done"). All four target files / components already exist from the prior steps: `frontend/src/test/merge-wizard.test.tsx` (Step 69, 10 cases) → `MergeWizard.tsx` 78.94 / 82.69 / 82.6 / 80.76 (statements / branches / functions / lines); `frontend/src/test/concordance-report.test.tsx` (Step 70) → `ConcordanceReport.tsx` 81.35 / 71.56 / 88.23 / 86; `frontend/src/test/variant-table-merge-filters.test.tsx` (Step 71, 8 cases) → `VariantTable.tsx` 91.55 / 88.11 / 82.05 / 91.66 (combined coverage with `variant-table.test.tsx`); `frontend/src/test/post-merge-rewatch.test.tsx` (Step 72, 10 cases) → `PostMergeRewatchModal.tsx` 91.04 / 85.71 / 90.9 / 93.44. The single gap surfaced by the coverage run was ConcordanceReport's branches metric at 67.64% — the existing 6 describes cover happy path, pagination, empty state, 423 stale-sample, and 404 not-merged, but no test exercises the path where provenance resolves OK while the report query itself fails with a non-423 error (the inline `<PageError>` branch at `ConcordanceReport.tsx:502-506`). Added one focused test case ("report-query 5xx handling" in `frontend/src/test/concordance-report.test.tsx`) that lets the provenance fetch succeed with `PROVENANCE_PAYLOAD` and returns a 500 on `reportUrl(0)`, asserting (a) the header + summary card still render (the page degrades gracefully on a partial-failure surface), (b) the error message "internal server error" surfaces in the table area via `<PageError>`, (c) the `concordance-discordant-table` testid is absent. The fix lifts ConcordanceReport branches from 67.64% to 71.56% — over the 70% floor — without touching any production code. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 Step 87 is a phase-boundary sweep step (Phase 3 frontend closure), so the full local sweep ran in this session: `npm test` ran green (59 files / 950 tests) and `pytest tests/backend/` ran green; `eslint` clean on the touched test file and `tsc --noEmit` clean. No production code touched in this step — the canonical Phase 3 frontend surfaces shipped in Steps 69 / 70 / 71 / 72 already meet DoD; Step 87 is the gate confirming that. The MRG-10 E2E in `tests/e2e/merge-samples.spec.ts` (Step 86) is the orthogonal cross-component coverage; this step is the per-component unit-test coverage.
- **Merge samples E2E (Step 86 / MRG-10; Plan §15.1):** New `tests/e2e/merge-samples.spec.ts` drives the canonical multi-source user journey end-to-end with a fully-mocked backend: `/individuals/{id}` lists both linked samples + a "Merge samples" CTA, the MergeWizard opens with `flag_only` selected by default, Preview renders the §10.4(c) concordance bucket counts, Confirm commits the merge + binds the returned `job_id` to the SSE annotation channel, a single `event: progress` payload with `status='complete'` lifts the gate and triggers the wizard's auto-redirect to `/?sample_id={merged}&post_merge=1&job_id={job}`, Dashboard renders the merged sample alongside the auto-opened `<PostMergeRewatchModal>` (re-watch candidate table with a disabled action on the source-private locus per the `canRewatch` rule), `/samples/{merged}/concordance` renders the paginated report with gene-context, and `/variants?sample_id={merged}` surfaces the Source + Concordance filter chips that Step 71 added. The spec patterns mocks via `page.route()` after `tests/e2e/individuals.spec.ts` (Step 57) for stateful samples / individuals / merge endpoints and after `tests/e2e/setup-wizard-lai.spec.ts` (Step 25) for the `text/event-stream` SSE route that ships a single terminal `progress` event. All API mocks use regex routes anchored on `(\?|$)` (or explicit slash terminators) so they don't accidentally intercept Vite dev-server source-module URLs like `/src/api/tags.ts` — `**/api/tags**` would otherwise greedy-match the trailing `.ts` and break the test's first page load.
- **MergeWizard ↔ Dashboard hand-off wiring (Step 86 scaffolding for MRG-10):** The MergeWizard component (Step 69) and PostMergeRewatchModal (Step 72) shipped without page-level integration; the canonical Plan §10.7 user flow ("Individual detail page gets a 'Merge samples' action" → "On redirect to the new sample's dashboard, `<PostMergeRewatchModal>` lists every `watched_variants` row…") was not yet reachable from the UI. The MRG-10 E2E necessarily closes that gap: (a) `frontend/src/pages/IndividualDetail.tsx` adds a "Merge samples" CTA (`data-testid="merge-samples-button"`) visible only when `linkedSamples.length === 2` (Plan §10.5 step 1 expects exactly two source ids) and inline-renders `<MergeWizard>` against the two linked samples; (b) `frontend/src/components/individuals/MergeWizard.tsx`'s auto-redirect now appends `post_merge=1` + the SSE `job_id` to the navigation URL so the Dashboard can pick up the redirect→modal hand-off; (c) `frontend/src/pages/Dashboard.tsx` reads `post_merge` + `job_id` from the URL and renders `<PostMergeRewatchModal>` when the flag is set, clearing both params on dismiss via `navigate({ search }, { replace: true })` so a refresh doesn't re-open the modal. The wiring is the minimum surface required to make the §10.7 user journey reachable from the UI; no semantics changed in either component (the wizard's preview/commit/SSE behaviour and the modal's annotation-gate logic are byte-identical to Steps 69 and 72).
- **Merge performance guard (Step 85 / MRG-09a; Plan §15.3 DoD, §16.5):** New `tests/backend/test_sample_merge_performance.py` (one slow-tier case, `@pytest.mark.slow`) wraps `backend.services.sample_merge.merge_samples` in a single `time.perf_counter()` window and asserts the WSL2 reference-machine budget of <30 s end-to-end for two 700 000-variant source samples. The timed window scopes to the merge service's measurable footprint — Plan §10.5 steps 1 – 8 — under the plan's "parse-from-DB + merge + write + annotate" rubric: step 3 (`_stream_raw_variants` on both source DBs) is the **parse-from-DB**, steps 2 + 4 (`_rsids_in_vep_bundle` conflict probe + `_apply_semantics` over the coord union) are the **merge**, steps 5 – 7 (insert `samples` row, materialise the per-sample DB via `create_sample_tables(..., is_merged_sample=True)` for the §10.4(a) `(chrom, pos)` PK, batch-write merged rows, write the single `merge_provenance` row) are the **write**, and step 8 (the Huey `create_annotation_job` + `run_annotation_task` enqueue, monkey-patched to a no-op here exactly as `test_sample_merge.py` / `test_sample_merge_full_pipeline.py` do) is the **annotate**. The terminal call lands on the enqueue rather than the synchronous annotation pass because production runs annotation *asynchronously* on the Huey worker pool — the user clicks "Merge", `merge_samples` returns as soon as the job is enqueued, and the SSE job channel streams annotation progress separately; treating the enqueue as the budget's terminal call matches the merge-service internals' own calibration (`_DURATION_BASELINE_SECONDS = 5` + `_DURATION_ROWS_PER_SECOND = 25_000` in `backend/services/sample_merge.py` project 33 s for a 700k-merged sample, the wizard's `est_duration_seconds`, anchored on this same 30 s perf envelope) and avoids conflating two distinct perf budgets — the synchronous annotation pass has its own slow-tier coverage in Step 42's `test_annotation_engine_ancestrydna_real_bundle.py` and `tests/backend/test_benchmark.py::test_annotation_600k_timing`. The drift design generates one base set via `scripts.benchmark.generate_raw_variants(700_000, seed=42)` for S1, then derives S2 by mutating 1% of genotypes to a guaranteed-different call (`TT`↔`GG`) and another ~1% to the `--` no-call sentinel on two interleaved cadences (`i % 100 == 0` discordance, `elif i % 50 == 0` no-call) so the §10.2 buckets land at ~98% match / ~1% discordant / ~1% filled_nocall with zero `unique_*` rows — the realistic AncestryDNA/23andMe overlap profile (~500k shared positions with small drift) at the upper end of the plan's 700k spec. Setup (variant generation, source-DB writes in 50k batches matching the production ingest path, registry construction) is intentionally excluded from the timed window because none of it runs when a user clicks "Merge" on samples that already exist. The `perf_registry` fixture mirrors the `merge_registry` pattern from Steps 65 / 83 — patches `backend.db.connection.get_settings` so the singleton resolves against `tmp_data_dir` and the staleness service reads from the same registry the merge service writes to; `database_versions['vep_bundle'].version = 'v2.0.0'` is pre-stamped so the §10.5 step 1 staleness guard passes (every source's `annotation_state.vep_bundle_version` is also `v2.0.0`). Post-merge assertions read back `raw_variants` (locks the `_SAMPLE_SIZE` row count — every coord shared between S1/S2 means zero `unique_*` rows and the merged row count equals the source row count exactly) and `merge_provenance` (locks the Plan §10.5 step 7 write). Wires into `.github/workflows/nightly.yml`: the cross-step ownership comment block drops the prior "(lands later)" qualifier on Step 85, and the auto-filed `slow-tier-regression` GitHub Issue body now lists the merge perf test alongside the LAI and ADNA real-bundle tests so triage routes to bio-validator / merge-service ownership instead of paging the wrong subagent. The test stays dormant on every PR-blocking run (the `slow` marker is the off-switch for the default test invocation; per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 targeted-test policy this is a Phase-3 cross-cutting timing guard but not in the full-sweep set — `pytest tests/backend/test_sample_merge_performance.py -m slow` runs the timing case standalone well under the 30 s budget locally). Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — a perf regression that pushed the merge over the budget would either degrade the user-visible merge wizard's `est_duration_seconds` estimate (`backend/services/sample_merge.py::_DURATION_BASELINE_SECONDS` + `_DURATION_ROWS_PER_SECOND` are calibrated against this same 700k×2 → <30 s envelope) or, worse, force a future maintainer to add a timeout that would silently truncate the merge mid-write and corrupt the `raw_variants` table; locking the envelope to a slow-tier guard surfaces the regression before either happens.
- **Merged-sample coverage telemetry shape (Step 84 / MRG-09b; Plan §5.6, §10.4(b), §10.5 step 5, §15.1):** Engine telemetry now emits the three-key uppercase `S1`/`S2`/`both` `by_source` payload for merged samples while preserving the existing single-key vendor shape for unmerged samples. `backend/annotation/engine.py::run_annotation` extends the per-sample `raw_variants` SELECT to include the Plan §10.4(b) `source` column (server-default `''` on unmerged samples, `'S1'`/`'S2'`/`'both'` on merged samples written by `backend/services/sample_merge.py::_apply_semantics`), snapshots `vep_data.keys()` *before* the Plan §5.1 coord-fallback augments the dict, and after the fallback buckets every batch row into a per-source counter under one of `vep_bundle_rsid_hits` / `vep_bundle_coord_fallback_hits` / `vep_misses` (the per-source value shape Plan §5.6 declares). The pre-fallback snapshot is load-bearing — without it the bucket attribution couldn't separate rsid hits from coord-fallback hits because both land in the same `vep_data` dict by the time the merge step runs. The new local `_bump_source` helper auto-creates a zero-initialized bucket on first sight of a source value so adding a future source token (or evolving the merge service's enum) doesn't require a parallel registration step here. `_build_coverage_stats` gains a `source_counters: dict[str, dict[str, int]] | None = None` keyword arg and a new branch keyed on `sample_metadata.file_format == 'merged_v1'` (Plan §10.5 step 5 — the canonical merged-sample token, inlined here as `_MERGED_FILE_FORMAT` rather than imported from `backend/services/sample_merge.py` to keep the engine free of services-layer imports): merged samples emit `by_source = {"S1": {...}, "S2": {...}, "both": {...}}` populated from `source_counters` (with `_zero_source_bucket()` fallbacks so every slot is emitted even when its bucket count is zero — Plan §5.6's "stable shape" contract for downstream consumers); unmerged samples take the existing single-key vendor branch unchanged, ignoring `source_counters` because every row carries the empty-string `source` default that would key into the same useless `""` bucket. The top-level rollup (`vep_bundle_rsid_hits` / `vep_bundle_coord_fallback_hits` / `vep_misses`) is computed from the engine-level totals identically across both branches, so the Plan §5.6 invariant "the top-level rollup is the sum across all `by_source` keys" holds in both cases — the unmerged branch trivially (one key) and the merged branch by construction (each row contributes to exactly one source bucket). New `tests/backend/test_annotation_engine_merged_telemetry.py` (8 cases across two classes) drives the MRG-09b contract end-to-end. `TestMergedSampleTelemetryShape` (7 cases) wires a `merged_sample_engine` fixture that builds a per-sample DB via `create_sample_tables(engine, is_merged_sample=True)` (Plan §10.4a `(chrom, pos)` PK), stamps `sample_metadata.file_format='merged_v1'` and seeds a `merge_provenance` row carrying a realistic `concordance_summary` JSON (`match=3, filled_nocall=0, discordant=1, unique_S1=2, unique_S2=2, collapsed_rsid=0`), then loads seven `raw_variants` rows hand-distributed across the three source values: two S1-only rsid-hitters (rs429358, rs4680), two S2-only rsid-hitters (rs7412, rs7903146), two `both` rsid-hitters (rs1801133, rs12913832), and one `both` row whose synthetic rsid `rs_unknown_locus` (chrom=99) misses both the rsid path and the coord-fallback so the `both` slot has a non-zero `vep_misses` count (without that miss the rollup-equality assertion would be satisfied trivially). The seven cases lock each MRG-09b sub-clause: (i) `test_by_source_is_three_key_uppercase` asserts `set(stats["by_source"].keys()) == {"S1", "S2", "both"}` and that each slot's value dict carries exactly `{vep_bundle_rsid_hits, vep_bundle_coord_fallback_hits, vep_misses}`; (ii) `test_by_source_counts_sum_to_total_variants` sums every bucket's three counts across all three sources and asserts the total equals `stats["total_variants"]` which equals `len(_MERGED_RAW_ROWS) == 7` — locks the §5.6 "every row contributes to exactly one source bucket" contract on the merged branch; (iii) `test_top_level_rollup_equals_sum_across_by_source` re-asserts the §5.6 rollup invariant in the merged branch (the existing `test_rollup_consistency` in `test_annotation_engine.py` only covers the unmerged branch); (iv) `test_by_source_keys_match_raw_variants_source_values` queries `SELECT DISTINCT source FROM raw_variants` and asserts the distinct values equal the `by_source` keys exactly — anchors the §10.4(b) enum to the §5.6 payload so a refactor that renamed a source token (or introduced a fourth value) would surface here rather than silently drifting the telemetry; (v) `test_by_source_keys_match_concordance_summary_suffix_tokens` reads `merge_provenance.concordance_summary`, extracts the suffixes after `unique_` (yielding `{"S1", "S2"}`), and asserts the suffix tokens are a strict subset of the `by_source` keys plus the `"both"` slot (which has no `unique_` analog because §10.2's "both" bucket folds the match + filled_nocall + discordant outcomes that touched both sources); (vi) `test_per_source_bucket_attribution_matches_rows` asserts the exact bucket counts per source (`S1: rsid=2 / coord=0 / miss=0`; `S2: rsid=2 / coord=0 / miss=0`; `both: rsid=2 / coord=0 / miss=1`) — locks the `_bump_source` placement so a future regression in the snapshot ordering (e.g., taking the rsid-hit snapshot *after* the coord-fallback) would visibly mis-attribute rows; (vii) `test_bundle_version_recorded` asserts the merged-sample payload still carries the stamped `bundle_version` from `database_versions['vep_bundle']`, since the merged/unmerged branching only swaps `by_source` and must leave the top-level keys (including `bundle_version`) untouched. `TestUnmergedSampleShapeRegression` (1 case) builds a sibling `unmerged_sample_engine` with the same seven rsids but stripped `source`/`concordance`/`alt_rsid`/`discordant_alt_genotype` columns (so they fall to their server-default empty strings) and `file_format='23andme_v5'`, runs `run_annotation`, and asserts the existing single-key vendor shape still holds (`by_source == {"23andme": {...}}` with the per-source dict matching the top-level rollup field-for-field) — locks the negative-branch invariant so the merged-sample dispatch can't accidentally claim every sample once a future refactor changes the branch predicate. The `registry` fixture mirrors `tests/backend/test_annotation_engine_merged_pk.py` (Step 78) — `MagicMock`-based `DBRegistry` exposing only VEP + reference engines (gnomAD/dbNSFP `RuntimeError` on access; the telemetry contract is independent of which optional sources are installed and skipping them keeps the fixture surface minimal). Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the targeted local-test policy applied (Step 84 is not in the cross-cutting full-sweep set, isn't an Alembic migration, and doesn't touch `backend/db/sample_schema.py` or `backend/db/tables.py`, but the engine change is load-bearing for every downstream caller of `run_annotation`); ran the new file (8 cases / 0.7 s) plus the engine-adjacent suite (`test_annotation_engine.py` + `test_annotation_engine_ancestrydna.py` + `test_annotation_engine_merged_pk.py` + `test_huey_annotation.py` + `test_annotation_state.py` — 125 cases / 25 s) plus the merge-adjacent suite (`test_sample_merge.py` + `test_sample_merge_preview.py` + `test_sample_merge_full_pipeline.py` + `test_sample_merge_commit_stale.py` + `test_sample_delete_cascade.py` + `test_sample_schema_migration_v7_v8.py` + `test_merge_routes.py` — 146 cases / 132 s) all green, and `ruff check backend/annotation/engine.py tests/backend/test_annotation_engine_merged_telemetry.py` is clean. Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — the merged-sample telemetry is what the post-merge admin panel (Settings → System Health) renders to surface "the merge actually improved coverage" and what `annotation_state.annotation_bundle_coverage_json` (Plan §7.4) persists for the Huey-task gate, so a silent shape drift between merged and unmerged samples would either break the admin surface or cause the stale-sample gate to mis-evaluate when comparing per-source coverage across re-annotations; R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) is the secondary item — `bundle_version` parity across the merged and unmerged branches is what makes the stale-sample dependency (`backend/api/dependencies.py::require_fresh_sample`) work uniformly for merged + unmerged samples after a bundle upgrade. No CLAUDE.md SOP #2 Context7 invocation needed: pure pytest + SQLAlchemy Core patterns already established throughout the existing engine + merge tests. No frontend changes, no OpenAPI / route surface changes, no migration. The follow-on Step 85 / MRG-09a lands the merge performance test (slow tier) asserting a 700k-variant merge completes in <30 s on the WSL2 reference machine.

- **Merged-sample full annotation pipeline + per-module sub-asserts (Step 83 / MRG-09; Plan §15.1):** New `tests/backend/test_sample_merge_full_pipeline.py` (5 cases in `TestMergedSampleFullPipeline`) drives the Plan §15.1 MRG-09 contract end-to-end: the test builds two source samples whose variant rows are split so each source carries only half the rsids any downstream module needs to surface a complete finding, runs `backend.services.sample_merge.merge_samples(..., FLAG_ONLY)` to produce a real `merged_v1` per-sample DB with the §10.4(a) `(chrom, pos)` PK + §10.4(b) `source`/`concordance`/`alt_rsid` provenance columns, runs `backend.annotation.engine.run_annotation` against the merged engine to populate `annotated_variants` (the contract MRG-09 names "merged sample runs full annotation pipeline"), then asserts each of the five sub-modules MRG-09 names: (i) **APOE both rsids resolved** — rs429358 lives only on S1 + rs7412 only on S2, each source alone surfaces `APOEStatus.MISSING_SNPS`, only after the merge unifies both rsids does `determine_apoe_genotype` return `APOEStatus.DETERMINED` with a well-formed ε-diplotype; (ii) **CPIC star-allele coverage delta** — S1 carries CYP2D6 *4's defining rsid (rs3892097) but not *2's (rs16947), S2 is the mirror image, each per-source `call_star_alleles_for_gene` result has exactly one defining rsid in `missing_rsids`, the merged call has `missing_rsids == set()` which is a strict subset of both source results (the coverage-delta invariant — "the merge actually improved pharmacogenomic coverage" rather than just stacking variant counts); (iii) **carrier-finding source attribution emitted** — a CFTR het Pathogenic ClinVar rsid (rs113993960) lives only on S2, `extract_carrier_variants(panel, merged_engine)` surfaces the carrier finding (gated by a single-row in-test backfill of `annotated_variants.zygosity='het'` — the annotation engine doesn't write that column today, matching the convention in `test_carrier_analysis.py`'s fixture which hand-seeds it identically), and the merged `raw_variants` row at the same rsid carries `source='S2' / concordance='unique'` so the post-merge UI can render the §10.4(b) provenance trail alongside the carrier finding — locks the provenance contract at the boundary where it matters most (carrier findings drive reproductive-counseling decisions, so the test asserts both columns the post-merge re-watch modal + UI would key off); (iv) **PRS CI re-validation within bounds** — a four-SNP synthetic PRS weight set whose rsids span both sources runs end-to-end on the merged sample's `annotated_variants`, `compute_prs` returns `coverage_fraction == 1.0 / snps_used == 4` (the merged sample has every weight-set rsid because both halves now live in one annotated table), `compute_prs_bootstrap_ci(..., rng_seed=42)` returns a well-formed interval with `lower ≤ percentile ≤ upper` both in `[0, 100]` and `bootstrap_iterations == 1000` (the production default); (v) **haplogroup tree-walk completes on merged chrM/chrY** — the merged raw_variants table carries chrM rsids (mt tree-walk) plus four chrY calls all typed + one non-PAR chrX homozygous call that drive Plan §9.4 sex inference to `XY` (which is what gates the Y tree-walk inside `assign_haplogroups`), both tree-walks return non-None `HaplogroupResult` instances without raising — the load-bearing invariant is "no exception" plus "both trees ran," not the specific haplogroup string (the synthetic rsids don't overlap with the real `haplogroup_bundle.json` on purpose so the tree-walk naturally terminates at the root with zero matched defining SNPs — exactly the production code path on sparse samples, where the alternative would be either a spurious assignment or an uncaught exception). The `merged_pipeline` fixture wires the full surface: a `merge_registry` fixture (mirroring `tests/backend/test_sample_merge.py`'s pattern) patches `backend.db.connection.get_settings` so the singleton-using `is_sample_stale` service inside `merge_samples` sees the test-scoped registry, pre-seeds the reference DB with ClinVar (CFTR rs113993960 Pathogenic) + CPIC alleles + diplotypes (CYP2D6 *1/*2/*4 with proper defining-variant JSON) + a `database_versions['vep_bundle']` row at `v2.0.0`, and materialises an on-disk `vep_bundle.db` at `settings.vep_bundle_db_path` with the production `vep_annotations` table shape + indices populated for the seven rsids the merged sample's `annotated_variants` row layer reads (APOE pair + the four PRS rsids + CFTR + the two CPIC rsids) — without seeding the bundle on disk before the registry's lazy `vep_engine` property opens it, `run_annotation` would silently lose its VEP_BIT contribution and the bundle-version row in `coverage_stats` would be `None`. The `_create_source_sample` helper sets up each source with `annotation_state['vep_bundle_version']='v2.0.0'` + `jobs.status='complete'` so the merge service's Plan §10.5 step 1 freshness + completion guards pass; `_noop_annotation_enqueue` no-ops `backend.tasks.huey_tasks.{create_annotation_job, run_annotation_task}` at the tail of `merge_samples` so the test can drive `run_annotation` explicitly (controlling the bundle surface — the production tail-enqueue would fire the full annotation+analysis pipeline through Huey which is too much side-effect for this test's surface). The annotation-error gate in the fixture filters out `gnomad ` / `dbnsfp ` prefixed errors (the on-disk empty SQLite files pass `_check_engine_available`'s `SELECT 1` probe but then surface "no such table" errors on the actual source lookup; MRG-09's sub-asserts only read columns populated by VEP + ClinVar so absent-source errors are expected and harmless), then asserts `result.rows_written > 0` to guarantee the annotation pass actually wrote at least one row before any sub-assert reads `annotated_variants`. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the targeted local-test policy applied (Step 83 is not in the cross-cutting full-sweep set — it's tests-only, doesn't alter any Alembic migration, and doesn't touch `backend/db/sample_schema.py` or `backend/db/tables.py`): ran the new file (5 cases / ~8 s) plus the merge-surface neighbour suite (`test_sample_merge.py` + `test_sample_merge_preview.py` + `test_alt_rsid_collapse.py` + `test_annotation_engine_merged_pk.py` + `test_tag_watch_non_propagation.py` + `test_sample_delete_cascade.py` — 102 cases / ~95 s) all green, and `ruff check tests/backend/test_sample_merge_full_pipeline.py` is clean. Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — MRG-09 is the broadest end-to-end seal on the merge contract because it exercises every analysis module the merged sample feeds into; the per-module sub-asserts collectively close the gap between "the merge service produced syntactically correct rows" (Steps 65, 66, 78, 79, 80, 81, 82) and "the merged sample actually drives each downstream module to a complete finding it couldn't have produced from either source alone" (the user-visible payoff the merge service was designed to deliver). R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) is the secondary item — the test runs `run_annotation` end-to-end on the merged sample and asserts the annotated_variants row layer feeds each module without divergence from the merged raw_variants base, locking the cross-PK contract from Step 78 / MRG-08c through to the consuming-module layer. R-04 (PRS bootstrap CI well-formedness) sits behind the PRS sub-assert; the `rng_seed=42` makes the test deterministic so a future regression in `compute_prs_bootstrap_ci` (e.g., off-by-one in the percentile computation, accidentally returning the raw score instead of the percentile, or breaking the `iterations == 1000` default) trips immediately. No CLAUDE.md SOP #2 Context7 invocation needed: pure pytest + SQLAlchemy Core + analysis-module call patterns already established throughout the existing merge tests. No backend or frontend production code touched, no OpenAPI / route surface changes, no migration. Tests-only step. The follow-on Step 84 / MRG-09b lands the merged-sample telemetry-shape test asserting `annotation_bundle_coverage_json.by_source` is three-key uppercase `S1`/`S2`/`both` post-merge with counts summing to `total_variants`.

- **Source-deletion cascade end-to-end test (Step 82 / MRG-08g; Plan §10.8, §15.1):** Extended `tests/backend/test_sample_delete_cascade.py` with a new `TestMergeThenDeleteCascade` class (4 cases) that drives the Plan §10.8 cascade through the real `backend.services.sample_merge.merge_samples` pipeline rather than the hand-built `merge_provenance` rows the Step 66 classes use. Each case (a) seeds an individual + two AncestryDNA-compatible source samples that satisfy every Plan §10.5 step 1 guard (`annotation_state['vep_bundle_version']='v2.0.0'`, completed annotation job, linked individual), (b) runs `merge_samples(..., strategy=FLAG_ONLY)` to produce a real `samples` row with `file_format='merged_v1'`, its `(chrom, pos)`-PK per-sample DB, and the production-shape `merge_provenance` payload, then (c) exercises `DELETE /api/samples/{id}` via the existing `client` TestClient fixture and asserts the cascade contract on the artefacts the production merge service emitted. `test_delete_source_cascades_to_real_merged_child` asserts the 204 response, that both the source reference row and the merged child reference row disappear from `samples`, that the on-disk `sample_*.db` files for both are unlinked, that the unrelated paired source survives untouched (row + on-disk file), and that the `sample_delete_cascade` structured-log line records `deleted_sample_id == source_id` plus `deleted_merged_children == [{"id": merged_id, "name": "Jane Doe (merged)"}]` — locks both deleted IDs in the audit trail as MRG-08g requires. `test_delete_other_source_also_cascades` provides the symmetric coverage that deleting *either* source ID (not just the first-position one) reaps the merged child, so a regression that accidentally keyed the cascade walk off `source_sample_ids[0]` only would trip immediately. `test_delete_unrelated_sample_does_not_cascade` is the negative half MRG-08g calls out explicitly: stands up an unrelated, unmerged sample under a different individual whose ID never appears in any `merge_provenance.source_sample_ids` JSON array, deletes it, and asserts (i) only the unrelated sample's reference row + on-disk file disappear, (ii) the merged child and both original sources remain present on disk and in `samples`, and (iii) the cascade log line still fires once but with `deleted_merged_children == []` — locks the contract that the `sample_delete_cascade` audit-log line is emitted on *every* DELETE (Plan §10.8 audit trail requirement), with the empty list distinguishing "no merged children to reap" from "cascade never walked". `test_merged_children_route_lists_real_merged_child` covers the preview-surface companion (`GET /api/samples/{id}/merged-children`) backing the Settings → Samples per-row delete confirmation dialog: both source IDs return `[{"id": merged_id, "name": "merged.txt"}]` and the merged sample itself returns `[]` (it is the child of the merge, not the source of one) — closes the gap between the cascade walk and the UI affordance that surfaces the cascade preview before the user confirms. The `_make_mergeable_source` helper assembles every Plan §10.5 step 1 guard (membership + status + freshness via `annotation_state` + `jobs.status='complete'`) so the merge orchestration's pre-write validation pass succeeds; the `_noop_annotation_enqueue` helper monkey-patches `backend.tasks.huey_tasks.{create_annotation_job, run_annotation_task}` to no-ops at the tail of `merge_samples` because the cascade contract is independent of whether the merged sample's post-merge annotation job actually ran — keeps each case <2 s by sidestepping the Huey worker plumbing. The shared `client` fixture (existing from Step 66) patches `backend.main.get_settings` + `backend.db.connection.get_settings` so the singleton-using `is_sample_stale` service inside `merge_samples` sees the same test-scoped `DBRegistry` that the TestClient sees — without that the freshness guard would mis-route `_read_installed_major` to the wrong reference DB and silently surface a stale-source 423 from inside the merge call rather than letting the cascade test reach its DELETE assertion. Test surface complements Step 66's contract-isolation suite (which hand-builds `merge_provenance` payloads to exercise `list_merged_children` + `delete_sample_with_cascade` in isolation from the merge service) and Step 79's tag/watch non-propagation test (which exercises the merge-write path but stops short of the deletion cascade) — together the three layers lock the full Plan §10.8 contract end-to-end. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the targeted local-test policy applied (Step 82 is not in the cross-cutting full-sweep set, isn't an Alembic migration, and doesn't touch `backend/db/sample_schema.py` or `backend/db/tables.py`): ran the modified file (20 cases / ~19 s) plus the merge-surface neighbour suite (`test_sample_merge.py` + `test_alt_rsid_collapse.py` + `test_merge_routes.py` — 75 cases / ~71 s) all green, and `ruff check tests/backend/test_sample_delete_cascade.py` is clean. Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — the cascade is what prevents a merged sample's `raw_variants` rows from outliving the source rows they were derived from, which would otherwise leave the user with orphaned findings whose provenance the registry can no longer resolve; R-07 (reference DB schema migration safety) is the secondary item — the cascade walk reads `merge_provenance.source_sample_ids` JSON arrays from per-sample DBs (not the reference DB), so a future migration that moves the column or renames the table without updating the cascade walk would trip this test before any user data was destroyed. No CLAUDE.md SOP #2 Context7 invocation needed: pure pytest + SQLAlchemy Core + FastAPI TestClient patterns already established throughout the existing merge tests. No backend or frontend production code touched, no OpenAPI / route surface changes, no migration. Tests-only step.
- **`alt_rsid` population on rsid collapse (Step 81 / MRG-08h; Plan §10.2 step 2, §10.4(b)–(c), §15.1):** New `tests/backend/test_alt_rsid_collapse.py` (4 cases across two classes) locks the Plan §10.4(b) `alt_rsid` column contract end-to-end on top of the unit-level tiebreaker coverage in `test_sample_merge.py::TestVepBundleTiebreaker`. The Step-65 merge service collapses two source rows at the same `(chrom, pos)` with different rsids to one row in the merged sample's `(chrom, pos)`-PK `raw_variants` table; the chosen rsid follows the §10.2 step 2 tiebreaker (bundle-hit wins, else S1 fallback) and the discarded rsid lands in the new `alt_rsid` column with server-default `''` at every locus that didn't collapse. `merge_provenance.concordance_summary.collapsed_rsid` counts the loci where the tiebreaker fired and must equal the number of merged rows with non-empty `alt_rsid` (Plan §10.4(c) additive-marker invariant). `TestCollapseUnderS1FallbackTiebreaker` (3 parameterised cases — one per Plan §10.3 strategy `flag_only` / `prefer_23andme` / `prefer_ancestrydna`) drives a six-locus dual-fixture with two collapse loci (`(1, 100)` same-genotype `→ match`, `(1, 200)` different alleles `→ discordant`) and four non-collapse loci (`(2, 300)` same-rsid match, `(2, 400)` same-rsid filled_nocall, `(3, 500)` unique-S1, `(3, 600)` unique-S2) so the assertion surface covers every Plan §10.2 bucket the `alt_rsid` invariant must hold across. With no VEP bundle seeded the bundle-membership probe returns the empty set, the §10.2 step 2 fallback fires, and S1's rsid wins at both collapse coords; the test asserts (i) exactly six rows exist on the merged `raw_variants` table (the two collapse loci yield one row each, locking the PK shape), (ii) `rsid` at `(1, 100)` is `rs100_s1` with `alt_rsid` `rs100_s2` and symmetrically at `(1, 200)`, (iii) every non-collapse locus has `alt_rsid == ''` regardless of which Plan §10.2 concordance bucket (match / filled_nocall / unique) it landed in — closes a gap the §10.2 step-2 verbiage could otherwise leave open (a future regression that defaulted `alt_rsid` to a copy of `rsid` on non-collapse rows would still pass the "row count = 6" assertion but would silently break the post-merge re-watch modal's `alt_rsid != ''` heuristic for surfacing discarded rsids), and (iv) `merge_provenance.concordance_summary.collapsed_rsid` equals `2` equals `sum(1 for r in rows if r.alt_rsid)`. Paired primary-partition invariant locks `match + filled_nocall + discordant + unique_S1 + unique_S2 == 6` so a future regression that mis-counted a collapsed row in two partitions trips immediately. Parameterising over strategies pins the orthogonality contract — the rsid-collapse tiebreaker is independent of the strategy axis: the strategy decides which genotype call wins at a discordant-alleles locus (Plan §10.3 table), the tiebreaker decides which rsid wins at a discordant-rsid coordinate (Plan §10.2 step 2), and `alt_rsid` reflects only the rsid-collapse axis. `TestCollapseUnderBundleHitTiebreaker` (1 case) drives the primary branch of the §10.2 step 2 tiebreaker by materialising a real `vep_bundle.db` at `settings.vep_bundle_db_path` (via the new `_seed_vep_bundle_rsids` helper) containing only S2's rsids at both collapse coords — the merge service's `_rsids_in_vep_bundle` probe resolves to S2 on both, flipping the winner; the test asserts `rsid == 'rs100_s2'` / `alt_rsid == 'rs100_s1'` at `(1, 100)` (symmetrically at `(1, 200)`) and that `concordance_summary.collapsed_rsid == 2 == count(alt_rsid != '')` still holds — the marker tracks the *fire* of the tiebreaker, not which side won. Materialising the bundle on disk before the `registry.vep_engine` property is first accessed is load-bearing: the lazy property opens a SQLite engine against `settings.vep_bundle_db_path`, and the empty-DB default (file absent, table absent) triggers the `merge_vep_bundle_unreachable` warning path that falls through to the S1 fallback — seeding the table before the merge runs is the only way to exercise the bundle-hit branch through `merge_samples` end-to-end. The seeded table is intentionally minimal (one `rsid TEXT` column) because `_rsids_in_vep_bundle` only `SELECT DISTINCT rsid FROM vep_annotations WHERE rsid IN (...)`s — it doesn't touch the annotation payload columns. Fixture surface mirrors `tests/backend/test_tag_watch_non_propagation.py` (Step 79) and `tests/backend/test_sample_merge.py` (Step 65) verbatim: the `merge_registry` fixture patches `backend.db.connection.get_settings` so `is_sample_stale` sees the test-scoped registry (the conftest `db_registry` fixture only builds an isolated registry without redirecting the singleton, which would mis-route `_read_installed_major` to the wrong reference DB and silently break the stale-source guard); `_create_individual` + `_create_source_sample` set up two sources linked to one individual with `status='complete'` and fresh `annotation_state['vep_bundle_version']='v2.0.0'` so the `merge_samples` staleness guard passes; `_seed_installed_vep_bundle` writes `database_versions['vep_bundle'].version='v2.0.0'` so the staleness service has something to compare against; `_noop_annotation_enqueue` replaces `backend.tasks.huey_tasks.{create_annotation_job, run_annotation_task}` with no-ops so the Huey enqueue at the tail of `merge_samples` doesn't fire and the test stays under 2 s per case. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the targeted local-test policy applied (Step 81 is not in the cross-cutting full-sweep set, isn't an Alembic migration, and doesn't touch `backend/db/sample_schema.py` or `backend/db/tables.py`): ran the new file (4 cases / ~5 s) plus the merge-surface neighbour suite (`test_sample_merge.py` + `test_sample_merge_preview.py` + `test_sample_merge_commit_stale.py` + `test_merge_routes.py` + `test_tag_watch_non_propagation.py` + `test_annotation_engine_merged_pk.py` + `test_sample_schema_migration_v7_v8.py` — 136 cases / ~119 s) all green, and `ruff check tests/backend/test_alt_rsid_collapse.py` is clean. Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — `alt_rsid` is the forensic trail for the rsid-collapse path, and the post-merge re-watch modal (MRG-13 / Step 72) keys off the column to surface discarded rsids that the source sample's `watched_variants` may have referenced (the non-propagation contract from Step 79 / MRG-08d is what makes a forensic trail necessary in the first place — without `alt_rsid` carrying the loser, a user who watched the discarded side of a collapse would have no way to find the variant on the merged sample); R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) is the secondary item — the cross-PK byte-identical annotation contract (Step 78 / MRG-08c) depends on `alt_rsid` being a write-only column that annotation never reads, which the §10.4(b) `server_default=''` declaration enforces structurally but only this end-to-end test exercises in practice. No CLAUDE.md SOP #2 Context7 invocation needed: pure pytest + SQLAlchemy Core patterns already established throughout the existing merge tests. No backend or frontend code touched, no OpenAPI / route surface changes, no migration. Tests-only step. The follow-on Step 82 / MRG-08g lands the source-deletion cascade test, asserting `DELETE /api/samples/{source_id}` removes the merged child + leaves the other source untouched + logs the cascade with both deleted ids.

- **Tag / watch non-propagation tests across the merge boundary (Step 79 / MRG-08d; Plan §10.4(a) invariant + commentary, §10.7, §15.1):** New `tests/backend/test_tag_watch_non_propagation.py` (5 cases across two classes) locks the Plan §10.4(a) contract that the four rsid-bearing per-sample tables (`annotated_variants`, `variant_tags`, `panel_coverage`, `watched_variants`) stay independent across a sample merge — the Step-65 merge service writes only `raw_variants` + `merge_provenance` into the freshly created merged sample DB, and any `variant_tags` / `watched_variants` rows authored on a source sample remain on that source DB rather than migrating to the merged child. The post-merge re-watch modal (MRG-13 / Step 72) is the user-facing surface that exposes the gap; this test step locks the no-propagation invariant *underneath* that surface so a future refactor of `merge_samples` can't accidentally copy tags/watches across (which would create stale rows referencing rsids that may not even appear on the merged sample, e.g. the discarded side of an rsid collapse). `TestPrivateRsidNonPropagation` (3 cases) drives the "AncestryDNA companion does not carry" wording from MRG-08d: (i) `test_unique_s1_rsid_tag_and_watch_stay_on_source` tags + watches `rs500` on the 23andMe leg (unique to S1, no chrom/pos collision with S2), runs `merge_samples` with `flag_only`, asserts the merged DB carries `rs500` in `raw_variants` (as `source='S1' / concordance='unique'` per Step 65 semantics) but its `variant_tags` and `watched_variants` tables are empty, and asserts the source's own rows survive intact post-merge — a paired sanity check that the merge pass doesn't accidentally *delete* tags/watches off the source either; (ii) `test_unique_s2_rsid_tag_and_watch_stay_on_source` is the symmetric S2 case, tagging `rs600` (unique to AncestryDNA) with the `Actionable` predefined tag + a watch row, asserting both stay on S2's DB and the merged DB stays empty; (iii) `test_merged_predefined_tags_seeded_but_no_variant_links` locks the seam between the two `tags`-family tables — `create_sample_tables` seeds the predefined `tags` rows (`Review later`, `Discuss with clinician`, `False positive`, `Actionable`, `Benign override`) on every fresh sample DB including merged ones, but the `variant_tags` join table starts empty regardless of the source's content. `TestRsidCollapseNonPropagation` (2 cases) drives the rsid-collapse leg of MRG-08d using the `(3, 700)` collapse locus where S1 carries `rs700_s1` and S2 carries `rs700_s2`: (i) `test_loser_side_tag_watch_does_not_migrate` tags + watches `rs700_s2` on S2 (the loser-side rsid — with no VEP bundle seeded, the Plan §10.2 step 2 tiebreaker falls back to S1, so merged.rsid = `rs700_s1` and merged.alt_rsid = `rs700_s2`); the test up-front asserts the collapse landed the way it expects (`rsid == 'rs700_s1' and alt_rsid == 'rs700_s2'`) so a future regression in the tiebreaker doesn't silently invalidate the no-propagation assertion, then asserts merged `variant_tags` + `watched_variants` are empty and S2's own rows survive — locks the explicit Plan §10.4(a) sentence: "A user who tagged or watched the discarded rsid in a source sample will not see those tags/watches transferred to the merged sample"; (ii) `test_winner_side_tag_watch_also_does_not_migrate` is the asymmetric companion — tags + watches `rs700_s1` on S1 (the *winning* rsid at the collapse), asserts the rsid IS present on merged `raw_variants` (because it won), but the merged DB's `variant_tags` + `watched_variants` are still empty because the four tables are independent across merges regardless of whether the source's rsid survives the collapse. The fixture (`linked_sources`) reuses the Step 65 / 77 helpers verbatim — `merge_registry` patches the `backend.db.connection.get_settings` singleton so `is_sample_stale` sees the test-scoped registry; `_create_individual` + `_create_source_sample` set up two sources linked to one individual with status=complete and fresh `annotation_state['vep_bundle_version']` so the `merge_samples` staleness guard passes; `_seed_installed_vep_bundle` + `_noop_annotation_enqueue` mirror the existing merge test scaffolding so the Huey enqueue at the tail doesn't fire and the staleness service compares against `v2.0.0`. New local helpers `_tag_variant` (looks up the predefined tag's id via the `tags` table and inserts a `variant_tags` row, mirroring `POST /api/tags/variant`) and `_watch_variant` (inserts a `watched_variants` row with a non-null `clinvar_significance_at_watch`, mirroring `POST /api/watches`) sit inline rather than escaping to a shared conftest because they're niche to this file — the surrounding tag-API and watches-API test files use TestClient round-trips through the live FastAPI app, which is heavier than this step needs. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the targeted local-test policy applied (Step 79 is not in the cross-cutting full-sweep set, isn't an Alembic migration, and doesn't touch `backend/db/sample_schema.py` or `backend/db/tables.py`); ran the new file (5 cases / ~7 s) and `ruff check tests/backend/test_tag_watch_non_propagation.py` is clean. Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — `variant_tags` and `watched_variants` are the user's annotations atop the variant catalog, and if they silently followed an rsid across a merge boundary the user would see tags/watches on a sample they never authored them on (or worse, on a discarded `alt_rsid` that doesn't even appear in the merged sample's variant table, which would surface as a phantom row in `GET /api/tags/variant/{rsid}` lookups); R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) is the secondary item — the post-merge re-watch modal's contract (MRG-13 / Step 72) depends on the merged sample's `watched_variants` table starting empty so the modal can populate it via explicit `POST /api/watches` mutations driven by the source's prior watch state. No backend or frontend code touched, no OpenAPI / route surface changes, no migration. Tests-only step. - **Annotation-engine cross-PK invariance test (Step 78 / MRG-08c; Plan §10.4(a) closing paragraph, §15.1):** New `tests/backend/test_annotation_engine_merged_pk.py` (6 cases across two classes) locks the AncestryDNA Plan §10.4(a) contract that ``run_annotation`` produces byte-identical ``annotated_variants`` regardless of the ``raw_variants`` PK shape — the merged-sample DB created via ``create_sample_tables(..., is_merged_sample=True)`` (Step 64) carries a ``(chrom, pos)`` PK while every other sample DB keeps the historical ``rsid`` PK, and the engine reads ``raw_variants`` by ``sa.select(...)`` rather than by PK lookup, so the swap must be invisible to annotation output. `TestPKDivergenceSanityChecks` (2 cases) up-front guard-rails the assertion: ``test_unmerged_has_rsid_pk`` confirms the default factory still emits ``rsid`` PK and ``test_merged_has_chrom_pos_pk`` confirms the merged factory emits ``(chrom, pos)`` PK — both fail loudly if a future refactor accidentally collapses the divergence (which would make the byte-identical comparison trivially pass on a single PK shape). `TestAnnotationCrossPKByteIdentical` (4 cases) drives the production ``run_annotation`` against two sibling sample DBs seeded with the same seven raw rows in the same order against the same in-memory VEP bundle (loaded from the canonical ``tests/fixtures/seed_csvs/vep_seed.csv``) + ClinVar-seeded reference DB (two rows so the ``annotation_coverage`` bitmask actually varies — ``VEP_BIT | CLINVAR_BIT`` on rs429358/rs1801133 vs. ``VEP_BIT`` alone on the other five — and the comparison exercises the merge path, not a single-bit constant): (i) ``test_annotated_variants_rows_are_byte_identical`` asserts the read-back rows (ordered by rsid for deterministic comparison) match dict-for-dict across all 7 loci × every column of the ``annotated_variants`` wide table; (ii) ``test_engine_result_counts_match`` asserts every ``AnnotationEngineResult`` field that drives downstream telemetry/SSE payloads agrees — ``total_variants``, ``rows_written``, ``vep_matched``, ``clinvar_matched``, ``gnomad_matched``, ``dbnsfp_matched``, ``gene_phenotype_matched``, ``vep_coord_fallback_matched`` — and that ``errors == []`` on both runs (a divergence here would surface as inconsistent SSE updates between merged and unmerged samples even if the on-disk rows happened to match); (iii) ``test_coverage_stats_match`` asserts the Plan §5.6 ``coverage_stats`` payload is identical and anchors the shape with ``bundle_version == "v2.0.0"`` + ``total_variants == 7`` + ``by_source`` keyed on ``"23andme"`` so a future refactor of ``_build_coverage_stats`` can't silently change what "byte-identical" claims to cover — both samples use ``file_format = "23andme_v5"`` so the vendor key derivation in ``_read_sample_file_format`` collapses to the same string; (iv) ``test_bitmask_actually_varies`` defends the test fixture itself by asserting the two ClinVar-hitting rsids produce ``VEP_BIT | CLINVAR_BIT`` and every other rsid produces ``VEP_BIT`` alone, so the byte-identical equality in case (i) is doing real merge-path comparison work rather than collapsing to equality on a single constant bitmask. Fixture surface mirrors `tests/backend/test_annotation_engine_ancestrydna.py` (Step 40) for consistency — ``StaticPool`` + ``check_same_thread=False`` in-memory SQLite engines so the engine's ``ThreadPoolExecutor`` can share connections across worker threads; ``MagicMock``-based ``DBRegistry`` exposing only VEP + reference engines (gnomAD/dbNSFP raise on access, mirroring a fresh install where the optional DBs haven't downloaded yet — the cross-PK contract holds independent of source count, and skipping the optional DBs keeps the fixture surface minimal). Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the targeted local-test policy applied (Step 78 is not in the cross-cutting full-sweep set, isn't an Alembic migration, and doesn't touch ``backend/db/sample_schema.py`` or ``backend/db/tables.py``); ran the new file (6 cases / 0.4 s) plus the neighbor suite (``test_annotation_engine.py`` + ``test_annotation_engine_ancestrydna.py`` + ``test_sample_schema_migration_v7_v8.py`` + ``test_sample_merge.py`` — 161 cases / 47 s) all green, and ``ruff check`` is clean. Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — every downstream analysis module that reads ``annotated_variants`` (cancer, cardiovascular, carrier_status, rare-variant finder) trusts annotation output to be a pure function of raw input + bundle state; a silent PK-induced divergence on merged samples would surface as different findings between merged and unmerged DBs over the same loci, which is exactly the data-integrity regression R-12 mitigates against. No CLAUDE.md SOP #2 Context7 invocation needed: pure pytest + SQLAlchemy Core patterns already established throughout the existing engine tests. Tests-only step — no backend or frontend code touched, no OpenAPI / route surface changes, no migration.
