- **Merge commit + concordance routes (Step 68 / MRG-04; Plan §10.6):** Three new routes wire the merge wizard's confirm step and post-merge review surface to the Step 65 / 67 service core. `POST /api/individuals/{id}/merge` on `backend/api/routes/individuals.py` accepts `{source_sample_ids, strategy, display_name}`, calls `backend.services.sample_merge.merge_samples`, and returns `{merged_sample_id, job_id}` with HTTP 201 — the `job_id` is read back from the `jobs` row the service writes via its local Huey enqueue (the route surfaces `''` when the enqueue branch logs and falls through so the wizard still gets a usable response). Error surface mirrors the preview route: 404 on unknown individual, 422 on shape / membership / status / empty-display-name failures (`InvalidMergeRequestError`), 423 on stale-source failures (`StaleSourceError`) with the structured Plan §7.5 payload. `GET /api/samples/{sample_id}/merge-provenance` on `backend/api/routes/samples.py` opens the per-sample DB read-only, returns the single `merge_provenance` row with `source_sample_ids` / `source_file_hashes` / `concordance_summary` JSON columns decoded, and 404s when the sample exists but isn't merged. `GET /api/samples/{sample_id}/concordance-report?limit=N&offset=K` returns `{concordance_summary, total_discordant, limit, offset, discordant_loci}` — `discordant_loci` is the paginated subset of `raw_variants WHERE concordance='discordant'`, LEFT-JOIN'd against `annotated_variants` for `gene_symbol` / `consequence` / `clinvar_significance` gene context (LEFT-JOIN tolerates pre-annotation reads + missing annotation rows). FastAPI `Query(ge=1, le=500, default=50)` + `Query(ge=0, default=0)` enforce the Plan §10.6 pagination bounds with native 422 on out-of-range values; rows are ordered by `(chrom, pos)` ascending. Both read routes declare `Depends(require_fresh_sample)` per the Plan §7.5 enumeration — the Step 12 drift guard at `tests/backend/test_stale_sample_dependency.py` already lists them in the `_SAMPLES_GATED_PATHS` set so no edits to the guard are needed in this step. The gate's documented contract (treat missing samples as `v1.0.0` per the §7.4 fallback) means a request for a nonexistent sample id on a gated route answers 423 rather than 404 — consistent with every other `Depends(require_fresh_sample)` route across the codebase. Pydantic models `MergeCommitRequest` / `MergeCommitResponse` / `MergeProvenanceResponse` / `ConcordanceReportResponse` / `DiscordantLocus` lock the surface; FastAPI generates the OpenAPI schema directly from them so no manual spec edit is needed. **Tests** land in a new `tests/backend/test_merge_routes.py` (19 cases): commit-route happy path, 404 / 422 / 423 plumbing including unlinked-samples and a stale-source rewrite of `annotation_state`; merge-provenance happy path with summary bucket counts matching the fixture, 404 on unmerged samples, 423 gate on stale samples; concordance-report happy path (single discordant locus with full gene context), pagination (offset past total → empty + correct `total_discordant`), `limit=501` / `limit=0` / `offset=-1` → 422 (FastAPI Query validation), 404 on unmerged, 423 on stale, summary parity with the provenance route. The merge service's Huey enqueue is stubbed with a deterministic `jobs` writer + an `annotation_state` upsert + `annotated_variants` writes so the gated reads exercise the full route surface against an isolated tmp-data-dir registry without firing the actual annotation pipeline. Touched: `backend/api/routes/individuals.py` (new `commit_merge_endpoint` + `MergeCommitRequest` / `MergeCommitResponse` + `_latest_annotation_job_id` helper + `merge_samples` import + `jobs` import), `backend/api/routes/samples.py` (new `get_merge_provenance` + `get_concordance_report` endpoints + `_read_merge_provenance` helper + response models + `require_fresh_sample` / `merge_provenance` / `raw_variants` / `annotated_variants` imports), `tests/backend/test_merge_routes.py` (new).
- **Merge concordance dry-run preview route (Step 67 / MRG-03; Plan §10.6):** New `POST /api/individuals/{id}/merge/preview` on `backend/api/routes/individuals.py` returns `{concordance_summary, est_duration_seconds}` without writing anything — backs the merge wizard's preview step (Plan §10.7 step 2). Wired through a new public `backend/services/sample_merge.py::preview_merge(registry, source_sample_ids, individual_id, strategy) -> dict` helper that shares the Step-65 orchestration via the new `_compute_merge_plan` pipeline: validation (count / distinct / strategy enum extracted into `_validate_request_shape`; existence / membership / annotation-completion / staleness extracted into `_validate_samples_and_freshness`) → open both source DBs read-only → stream `raw_variants` into the `(chrom, pos)`-keyed map → probe the VEP bundle for the conflict-rsid subset → apply §10.2 / §10.3 semantics. Both `merge_samples` and `preview_merge` now call this shared helper so the preview/commit split exercises the exact same validation surface and semantics — the only difference is what happens after the plan is computed (write per-sample DB + provenance + enqueue annotation on commit, vs. package the summary + duration estimate on preview). `merge_samples`'s display-name check moves up to land before `_compute_merge_plan` (preview doesn't take a display_name; the wizard fills that in only on the confirm step); every existing `test_sample_merge.py` validation case continues to surface the same exception with the same matcher. `est_duration_seconds` is computed by `_estimate_duration_seconds(len(merged_rows))` = `5 + (rows // 25_000)` — a 5-second baseline absorbs annotation-queue overhead and the 25k-rows/sec amortisation matches the Step 85 / MRG-09a perf budget (700k variants land in <30 s on the WSL2 reference machine, so the estimate returns 33 s for a 700k merge). Route plumbing: `MergePreviewRequest{source_sample_ids: list[int] (min_length=2, max_length=2), strategy: Literal["prefer_23andme","prefer_ancestrydna","flag_only"]}` and `MergePreviewResponse{concordance_summary: dict[str, int], est_duration_seconds: int}` pydantic models — FastAPI's pydantic layer rejects mis-shaped bodies with 422 before the service runs. The route calls `_require_individual` first so a nonexistent individual surfaces 404, then catches `InvalidMergeRequestError` → 422 and `StaleSourceError` → 423 (body carries the structured `{error, stale_sample_ids, message, reannotate_url}` payload Plan §7.5 declares for `require_fresh_sample`, so the wizard renders the re-annotate banner with the same shape it does for stale-sample dependency drift). Tested in two existing files (the exhaustive surface — happy-path bucket counts against the hand-curated dual-upload fixture, missing-`annotation_state` fallback to v1.0.0, source-status-not-complete payload, mismatched-individual → 422, single-source → 422, invalid-strategy → 422, stale-source → 423 — lives in the upcoming `tests/backend/test_sample_merge_preview.py` in Step 73 / MRG-03a): (i) `tests/backend/test_sample_merge.py::TestPreviewMerge` grew six cases — `_estimate_duration_seconds` returns the 5 s floor at zero rows; 25 k rows → 6 s; 700 k rows → 33 s; the helper round-trips through the same 7-locus dual-fixture the Step 65 happy-path tests use and returns the same `{match: 2, filled_nocall: 2, discordant: 1, unique_S1: 1, unique_S2: 1, collapsed_rsid: 1}` summary the commit path writes into `merge_provenance` (locks the helper-split contract — preview and commit observe identical semantics); the snapshot pre/post `samples` count + on-disk `sample_*.db` file list assertion proves the dry-run writes nothing; `_validate_request_shape` propagates `InvalidMergeRequestError` through the helper unchanged; `_validate_samples_and_freshness` propagates `StaleSourceError` with the stale-sample-ids attribute through the helper unchanged. (ii) `tests/backend/test_individuals_routes.py::TestMergePreviewRoute` grew four route-plumbing cases — 404 on nonexistent individual (the `_require_individual` check fires before the service is touched); 422 on a `bogus_strategy` value (pydantic Literal rejection before the service runs); 422 on a single-id source list (pydantic `min_length=2` rejection before the service runs); 422 with "not linked" in the detail string when the request targets samples whose `individual_id` is NULL (the §10.5 step-1 membership failure surfaces through `_validate_samples_and_freshness`'s "sample {sid} is not linked to individual {id}" message). The route happy-path payload assertion against a hand-curated dual-upload fixture is the dual-upload fixture's job in Step 75 / MRG-08 (the fixture lands then; testing the wire-level payload before that would duplicate scope into this step). Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the targeted local-test policy applied (Step 67 is not in the cross-cutting full-sweep set, isn't an Alembic migration, and doesn't change `backend/db/sample_schema.py` or `backend/db/tables.py`); `pytest tests/backend/test_sample_merge.py tests/backend/test_individuals_routes.py tests/backend/test_no_call_sentinel_parity.py tests/backend/test_sample_delete_cascade.py` ran green (69 + 23 + 32 + 16 = 140 cases) and `ruff check backend/services/sample_merge.py backend/api/routes/individuals.py tests/backend/test_sample_merge.py tests/backend/test_individuals_routes.py` is clean. Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — the preview step is the user's only chance to inspect the concordance bucket counts before committing to a merge, and the helper-split contract (preview observes the exact same semantics as commit) is what makes the wizard's "what you see is what you'll get" promise hold; the same `_compute_merge_plan` pipeline writes the bucket counts that the commit-path writes into `merge_provenance.concordance_summary`. R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) is the secondary item — the 423 stale-source payload shape matches `require_fresh_sample` exactly, so the wizard's stale-sample banner renders identically whether the staleness was detected by the route gate (Step 12 / `Depends(require_fresh_sample)`) or by the merge service's own freshness check (Step 65 / `is_sample_stale` integration). No frontend changes — Step 69 will add the `<MergeWizard>` component that calls this route. No CLAUDE.md SOP #2 Context7 invocation needed: this step only uses existing FastAPI / pydantic / SQLAlchemy patterns already established throughout the file (HTTPException, APIRouter, Field, Literal, BaseModel, `sa.select`), no new library or framework surface introduced.
- **Source-deletion cascade (Step 66 / MRG-02a; Plan §10.8):** New `backend/services/sample_delete.py` centralises the cascade walk that every `DELETE /api/samples/{id}` path now invokes: deleting a sample referenced by any `merge_provenance.source_sample_ids` JSON array fires a single-confirmation cascade that destroys every merged child (DB file then reference row) before tearing down the source. Public surface: `MergedChild(id, name)` dataclass, `DeleteCascadeResult(deleted_sample_id, deleted_sample_name, deleted_merged_children)` dataclass, `list_merged_children(registry, sample_id) -> list[MergedChild]`, `delete_sample_with_cascade(registry, sample_id) -> DeleteCascadeResult | None` (returns `None` when the row does not exist so the caller can surface 404). The traversal is O(N) over `samples.file_format == 'merged_v1'` because `merge_provenance` is a single-row table inside each merged sample's per-sample DB (Plan §10.4c), not the reference DB — real installs carry a handful of merged samples so the one-open-per-merged-sample pass is acceptable. Defensive contract: a merged child whose DB file is missing on disk logs `merged_sample_db_missing` (WARNING) and is skipped; a merged child whose `merge_provenance.source_sample_ids` is unparseable JSON logs `merged_provenance_malformed` and is skipped; a merged child whose per-sample DB throws while opening logs `merged_provenance_read_failed` and is skipped — the deletion walk never raises on a half-broken install because the single-confirmation cascade in the UI is the only place a user can recover the orphaned rows from. Cascade ordering (Plan §10.8): merged-child DB file first, merged-child reference row second, source DB file third, source reference row last — a crash mid-cascade leaves the worse failure mode (merged sample claiming sources that are gone) impossible because the source reference row is always the last write. The route layer (`backend/api/routes/samples.py`) was rewired in two places: (a) `DELETE /api/samples/{sample_id}` now delegates entirely to `delete_sample_with_cascade`, dropping its inline `samples.delete()` + WAL/SHM cleanup (the cleanup is now centralised in the service's `_delete_sample_files` helper, which calls `registry.dispose_sample_engine` + `Path.unlink(missing_ok=True)` for the `.db`, `-wal`, and `-shm` siblings); (b) a new `GET /api/samples/{sample_id}/merged-children` route surfaces the cascade preview as `list[MergedChildResponse{id, name}]` so the frontend can render the impact before the user commits — 404 when the sample doesn't exist, `[]` when the sample has never been merged. Frontend (`frontend/src/components/settings/SampleMetadataEditor.tsx::DeleteSampleConfirm`) consumes the preview via a new `useSampleMergedChildren(sampleId)` hook in `frontend/src/api/samples.ts` (React Query, `staleTime: 0` so a re-merge between delete attempts is reflected immediately) and renders a cascade-warning block (`data-testid="delete-cascade-{id}"`) only when `cascadeCount > 0`: count + grammar (singular `merged sample` vs plural `merged samples`), bullet list of merged-child names (`data-testid="delete-cascade-child-{childId}"`), and an explanatory line that those merged samples cannot be reconstructed without the source. The confirm button rewrites from `Delete Sample` to `Delete Sample + N Merged` so the cascade is unmissable in the click target itself, and stays disabled while the preview query is loading (`Checking for merged samples…` placeholder). The DELETE mutation still fires exactly once regardless of cascade size — the backend service does the walk transactionally so the route stays a single HTTP call. New `MergedChild` type added to `frontend/src/types/samples.ts`. Tested in the new `tests/backend/test_sample_delete_cascade.py` (16 cases across four classes): `TestListMergedChildren` (5 cases — empty list when never merged; happy-path lists single merged child by id + name; both sources point to the same merged child symmetrically; missing-DB-file path returns `[]` + logs `merged_sample_db_missing`; malformed-JSON path returns `[]` + logs `merged_provenance_malformed`); `TestDeleteSampleWithCascade` (5 cases — unmerged delete returns `deleted_merged_children == []` and removes only the source; merged-source delete removes source + every merged child but spares the other source; `None` returned for nonexistent sample; INFO log `sample_delete_cascade` carries `deleted_sample_id` + `deleted_merged_children=[{id,name}]` as structured attributes; unmerged delete produces a log entry with an empty `deleted_merged_children` list); `TestMergedChildrenRoute` (3 cases — `[]` for unmerged sample, populated list for source of a merge, 404 for missing sample); `TestDeleteRouteCascade` (3 cases — DELETE 204 cascades through to reference DB so the merged child id is gone; DELETE 204 on an unmerged sample; 404 for missing sample). Tests are self-contained — every merged child is materialised by hand (samples row + per-sample DB with `merge_provenance` row written via `create_sample_tables(is_merged_sample=True)` from Step 64) so the cascade walk is exercised in isolation from the full Step 65 merge orchestration; the end-to-end merge → delete → cascade flow through `merge_samples` itself lands in Step 82 (MRG-08g). Test fixture `cascade_registry` mirrors `test_sample_merge.py::merge_registry` — `patch("backend.db.connection.get_settings", return_value=settings)` + `reset_registry()` so the route's `get_registry()` singleton points at `tmp_data_dir`. Frontend coverage in `frontend/src/test/sample-metadata-editor.test.tsx` grew four cascade-focused cases — no-cascade block hidden when API returns `[]`; cascade renders count + names + plural copy; singular copy for exactly one merged child; single DELETE issued on confirm regardless of cascade size. The shared `makeRouter` helper gained `mergedChildren` and `deleteSample` handlers so the existing delete-confirmation tests (which now also fire the preview query) stay green without per-test boilerplate. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the cross-cutting full-sweep gate ran (`pytest tests/backend/` — flagged ⚠ full-sweep because the cascade walk is the centralised contract every DELETE-sample path uses, and a regression in any sample-scoped route's delete handler would silently revert the cascade). Risk register R-12 (data-integrity / genotype concordance) is the load-bearing item: orphaning a merged sample (its source rows gone) silently produces nonsensical analysis findings — the cascade is the entire defence and the ordering invariant (merged-child rows always go before source rows) is locked by the `TestDeleteSampleWithCascade::test_cascade_removes_merged_child_when_source_deleted` row-count assertion. R-15 (storage integrity) defends the WAL/SHM cleanup — the service centralises the `Path(f"{db_path}-wal").unlink(missing_ok=True)` / `-shm` siblings removal that was previously inlined per-route, so any future route gaining a sample-delete path inherits the cleanup automatically. R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) is a secondary item: a merged sample whose source the user deleted would still pass `require_fresh_sample` on its own annotation provenance, but its `raw_variants` rows refer to source provenance the registry no longer has — the cascade prevents that ambiguous state from ever existing in the first place.
- **Sample-merge service core (Step 65 / MRG-02; Plan §10.2, §10.5):** New `backend/services/sample_merge.py::merge_samples(registry, source_sample_ids, individual_id, strategy, display_name) -> int` materialises a merged per-sample DB from two source samples linked to the same `individuals` row, returning the new `samples.id`. Pipeline (Plan §10.5 steps 1–8): (1) validation — `source_sample_ids` must list exactly two distinct ids; both must resolve to a `samples` row whose `individual_id` matches the request; both samples' most-recent `jobs` row with `job_type='annotation'` must carry `status='complete'`; neither may be stale per `backend.services.staleness.is_sample_stale` — membership / status / shape failures raise `InvalidMergeRequestError` (the Step 68 route maps to HTTP 422); stale-source raises `StaleSourceError` carrying `{error: 'stale_source_sample', stale_sample_ids: [...], message, reannotate_url}` (the Step 68 route maps to HTTP 423, same shape Plan §7.5 declares for `require_fresh_sample`); (2) open both source DBs read-only through `registry.get_sample_engine` and stream `raw_variants` into a `(chrom, pos)`-keyed in-memory map (~840 k loci × ~80 bytes ≈ 80 MB peak per source, acceptable per Plan §10.5 step 3); (3) collect the conflict-rsid subset (loci where both sources are present with different rsids — typically <1% of total loci) and probe `vep_annotations.rsid` via `registry.vep_engine` exactly once per probe batch (`_VEP_BUNDLE_PROBE_BATCH = 500`, under SQLite's 999-variable limit); a missing or unreachable bundle file logs `merge_vep_bundle_unreachable` and falls through to the §10.2 step 2 "both or neither in bundle → prefer S1" branch, so merge keeps working on machines that haven't installed the ~600 MB Step-4 bundle yet; (4) apply §10.2 / §10.3 semantics in `_apply_semantics`: unique-to-S1 → `(source='S1', concordance='unique', alt_rsid='')`, unique-to-S2 → symmetric; same coordinate both sides → rsid-collapse tiebreaker first (bundle-hit wins, then S1 fallback, with the losing rsid written to `alt_rsid` and `concordance_summary.collapsed_rsid` incremented as an additive marker per Plan §10.4c), then genotype concordance — both no-call → `match` (round-trips through `is_no_call` so downstream findings stay suppressed), exactly one no-call → `filled_nocall` with `source` pointing at the calling side, both called and equal → `match` with `source='both'`, both called and discordant → strategy decides (`FLAG_ONLY` writes `genotype='??'` and `discordant_alt_genotype='S1=<s1_gt>;S2=<s2_gt>'`; `PREFER_23ANDME` / `PREFER_ANCESTRYDNA` resolve the winner by reading each sample's `file_format` prefix and write `discordant_alt_genotype='S<loser>=<loser_gt>'`). Output rows are sorted `(chrom, pos)` so test assertions are deterministic and bulk inserts land in PK order; (5) compute `file_hash = SHA-256(S1.file_hash | S2.file_hash | strategy.value | SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION)` per Plan §10.5 step 5 — order-sensitive (rsid tiebreaker prefers S1) so `[A,B]` and `[B,A]` yield distinct hashes, and `SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION` is included so a re-merge after a future schema bump produces a distinct hash; the helper `_compute_file_hash` is exposed for the Step 77 re-merge / hash-invariants test; (6) insert the new `samples` row with `file_format='merged_v1'`, `individual_id` propagated, allocate the id, then update `db_path = f"samples/sample_{id}.db"`; (7) **pre-create** the merged sample DB on a throwaway `sa.create_engine(...)` (not the registry's cached engine) so `create_sample_tables(bootstrap_engine, is_merged_sample=True)` from Step 64 materialises `raw_variants` with the `(chrom, pos)` PK *before* `registry.get_sample_engine` is invoked — otherwise the registry's `ensure_sample_schema_current` would materialise the default rsid-PK layout first and collide with the merged DDL; (8) write `sample_metadata` (single-row), the single-row `merge_provenance` (`{id=1, strategy, source_sample_ids=JSON [s1, s2], source_file_hashes=JSON, concordance_summary=JSON {match, filled_nocall, discordant, unique_S1, unique_S2, collapsed_rsid}}` enforcing Plan §10.4c's row-count invariant: `match + filled_nocall + discordant + unique_S1 + unique_S2 == total merged loci`), and bulk-insert `raw_variants` in 10 k-row batches matching the file-ingest path; (9) lazy-import `backend.tasks.huey_tasks.{create_annotation_job, run_annotation_task}` and enqueue the standard annotation job against `new_sample_id` — the caller polls existing `GET /api/annotation/status/{job_id}`. An enqueue failure is logged (`merge_annotation_enqueue_failed`) but never rolls back the merge, since the merged sample is intact on disk and the user can retry via `POST /api/annotation/{sample_id}`. Public surface: `merge_samples`, `MergeStrategy` (StrEnum: `PREFER_23ANDME`, `PREFER_ANCESTRYDNA`, `FLAG_ONLY`), `MergeError` / `InvalidMergeRequestError` / `StaleSourceError`, `_compute_file_hash` (exposed for test parity with the Plan §10.5 step 5 recipe). Tested in `tests/backend/test_sample_merge.py` (25 cases across eight classes, all green): `TestHappyPath` (7 cases over a 7-locus dual-fixture exercising every §10.2 bucket — match at same-rsid/same-call, filled_nocall in both directions, discordant under all three strategies, unique-to-S1 / unique-to-S2, and different-rsid-same-coordinate collapse; concordance_summary counts (`match=2, filled_nocall=2, discordant=1, unique_S1=1, unique_S2=1, collapsed_rsid=1`) match the bucket constructions exactly and sum to `len(rows) == 7`; `prefer_23andme` keeps S1's call at the discordant locus with `discordant_alt_genotype="S2=GG"`; `prefer_ancestrydna` symmetric with `discordant_alt_genotype="S1=AA"`; new samples row carries `individual_id` + `file_format='merged_v1'` + `db_path=samples/sample_<id>.db` and the file exists on disk; merged DB's `raw_variants` PK is `(chrom, pos)`; `merge_provenance.source_sample_ids/source_file_hashes` JSON round-trips); `TestFileHashRecipe` (4 cases — deterministic, order-sensitive, distinct per strategy, and an explicit `hashlib.sha256(f"a|b|flag_only|{SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION}".encode()).hexdigest()` recomputation that pins the exact payload contract so a future bump trips before silently producing colliding hashes across versions); `TestValidation` (6 cases — wrong source count, duplicate source ids, missing/whitespace display_name, sample-not-found, sample linked to a different individual, source annotation in `running` state); `TestStaleSource` (1 case — installed `v2.0.0` + S2 recorded as `v1.0.0` → `StaleSourceError(stale_sample_ids=[s2_id], detail={error: 'stale_source_sample', ...})` with `"Re-annotate"` in the message); `TestNoProductionSideEffects` (1 case — an `InvalidMergeRequestError` leaves zero `samples` rows and no `sample_*.db` files on disk, locking transactional cleanliness on the early-exit path); `TestVepBundleTiebreaker` (3 cases driving `_apply_semantics` directly — S1-rsid in bundle wins over S2, S2-rsid in bundle wins over S1, neither in bundle falls back to S1; pure-function tests so no real ~600 MB bundle on disk is required); `TestAnnotationEnqueue` (2 cases — `monkeypatch` captures the `(sample_id, job_id)` pair passed to both `create_annotation_job` and `run_annotation_task` and asserts both fire with the new merged sample id; a second case raises `ValueError` from `create_annotation_job` and asserts the merge still persists + the warning lands in `caplog`); `TestEmptySourcesEdgeCase` (1 case — two empty source DBs → merged sample with zero `raw_variants` rows and an all-zero concordance summary). The test file ships a custom `merge_registry` fixture mirroring `tests/backend/test_staleness.py::staleness_env` — `patch("backend.db.connection.get_settings", return_value=settings)` + `reset_registry()` so the staleness service's `get_registry()` singleton points at `tmp_data_dir` (the conftest `db_registry` fixture only builds an isolated registry and doesn't redirect the singleton, which would cause `_read_installed_major` to read from the wrong reference DB and short-circuit the stale-source check). Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the cross-cutting full-sweep gate ran (`pytest tests/backend/` — flagged ⚠ full-sweep because the merge service creates merged sample DBs that downstream analysis modules must read identically; the byte-identical cross-PK read contract is locked by `test_standard_reader_returns_rows_from_both` in Step 64 and the no-call sentinel adoption from Steps 60–62 already pins the `'??'` flag-only output as transparent to every analysis module). Risk register: R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item — `_apply_semantics` is the entire concordance contract Phase 3 is built around and every bucket maps to a Plan §10.2 / §10.3 line, with the strategy / no-call / discordance matrix locked by `TestHappyPath` + `TestVepBundleTiebreaker`. R-15 (data-integrity / storage) defends the file_hash recipe — including `SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION` in the SHA-256 payload is the guard against a v8→v9 bump silently re-producing a v8 hash, locked explicitly by `TestFileHashRecipe::test_compute_file_hash_includes_schema_version`. R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) is the secondary item — the merged sample re-enters the standard annotation cascade as a normal sample (the engine reads `raw_variants` by SELECT, not by PK lookup, so the `(chrom, pos)` PK is invisible to it) and the post-Step-65 step 78 cross-PK test (`test_annotation_engine_merged_pk.py`) closes the loop. The dry-run preview split Step 67 will introduce is intentionally not in scope here: the orchestration is a single end-to-end function for now; Step 67 will pull a `dry_run: bool` flag (or a split helper) through this function once the preview route lands. No frontend changes — the Step 69 merge wizard and Step 68 routes consume this service via the future API surface.
- **`is_merged_sample` factory parameter on `create_sample_tables` (Step 64 / MRG-01 part 2; Plan §10.4a):** `backend/db/sample_schema.py::create_sample_tables` grows a keyword-only `is_merged_sample: bool = False` argument that selects the `raw_variants` primary-key layout at table-creation time. Default (`False`) keeps the historical `rsid` PK every single-vendor sample DB has used since v1 — covers regular file ingest (`backend/api/routes/ingest.py:156`), every test fixture (`tests/backend/conftest.py:48` `sample_engine`, `test_haplogroup.py`, `test_stale_sample_dependency.py`), and every other pre-Phase-3 caller without modification. Passing `is_merged_sample=True` (only `backend/services/sample_merge.py` will do this, landing in Step 65) materialises `raw_variants` with a composite `PRIMARY KEY (chrom, pos)` because the canonical merge key from Plan §10.2 is the coordinate pair (two source samples carrying different rsids at the same `(chrom, pos)` collapse to one row; rsid would have produced an artificial dup-or-drop). The four v8 provenance columns (`source`, `concordance`, `discordant_alt_genotype`, `alt_rsid`) ship in both DDL paths so a downstream `INSERT` doesn't have to branch by sample type. Implementation strategy: rather than the Plan-§10.4a "fresh `MetaData()` per call" sketch (which would force redefining 13+ unrelated tables per sample-DB open), the merged-PK branch issues a single raw `CREATE TABLE raw_variants ... PRIMARY KEY (chrom, pos)` DDL *before* `sample_metadata_obj.create_all(engine, checkfirst=True)` runs — `checkfirst=True` then sees `raw_variants` already exists and skips it, while still creating every other table (`annotated_variants`, `merge_provenance`, `annotation_state`, `tags`, `watched_variants`, `findings`, `apoe_gate`, `haplogroup_assignments`, `lai_results`, `panel_coverage`, `variant_tags`, `variant_overlays`) from the module-level metadata. The redundant `idx_raw_chrom_pos` index that `create_all` also issues against the (already PK-indexed) `(chrom, pos)` pair is harmless on SQLite (verified by an inspector smoke test — the explicit index coexists with the autoindex for the PK). Per Plan §10.4a invariant, only `raw_variants` swaps its PK — `annotated_variants` keeps `rsid` PK (annotation engine upserts via `index_elements=["rsid"]` and merged samples carry one rsid per locus from the §10.2 collapse, so writes succeed unchanged), `variant_tags` keeps composite `(rsid, tag_id)`, `panel_coverage` keeps `(module, rsid)`, and `watched_variants` keeps `rsid`. The v7→v8 in-place upgrade path (`ensure_sample_schema_current` → `_add_missing_columns`) is intentionally unchanged: Plan §10.4 final paragraph locks "The (chrom, pos) PK divergence does not apply to in-place v7→v8 upgrades" — every existing single-vendor DB keeps rsid PK forever, the new PK only takes effect on freshly-created merged-sample DBs that the Step 65 merge service produces. Standard readers continue to work transparently against either layout because the module-level `raw_variants` Table object is referenced for its columns (`raw_variants.c.rsid`, `.c.chrom`, `.c.pos`, `.c.genotype`) in `sa.select(...)` calls throughout `backend/annotation/{clinvar,vep_bundle,dbsnp,vcfanno_runner}.py` and `backend/ingestion/vcf_export.py` — PK is a constraint, not a query requirement, so the select round-trips identical rows from both PK variants (locked by `test_standard_reader_returns_rows_from_both`). Tested in `tests/backend/test_sample_schema_migration_v7_v8.py::TestIsMergedSampleFactory` (9 cases, all green): default omitting the flag → rsid PK; explicit `is_merged_sample=False` → rsid PK; `is_merged_sample=True` → `(chrom, pos)` PK; merged DB carries the full v8 surface (four provenance columns + `merge_provenance` table + `annotated_variants` still rsid-PK as the negative cross-table assertion); merged DB stamped at `SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION == 8`; PK swap proven from both sides — merged DB rejects two different-rsid rows at the same `(chrom, pos)` with `IntegrityError` (locks the new PK fires) and accepts two same-rsid rows at different coordinates (would have failed under the old rsid PK; locks the swap is real, not just additive); unmerged-default negative-control still rejects duplicate-rsid inserts (regression boundary — `is_merged_sample=False` must not silently lift the old constraint); and the standard-reader round-trip across both PK variants returns byte-identical row sets via the module-level `raw_variants` Table import. Total file is now 23 cases up from 16. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the cross-cutting full-sweep gate ran (`pytest tests/backend/` — flagged ⚠ full-sweep because the `raw_variants` PK branches on a factory parameter and every reader / writer must still work both ways). Risk register R-15 (data-integrity) is the load-bearing item: the PK swap is the storage layer the Step 65 merge service writes into, and the constraint-not-query-requirement contract — proven by the byte-identical select round-trip — keeps every annotation reader untouched. R-12 (genotype concordance) is the secondary item: the `(chrom, pos)` PK is what makes a different-rsid-same-coordinate collapse a hard rejection at INSERT time rather than a silent dedup-or-shadow at SELECT time, surfacing inconsistent source-sample provenance to the merge service explicitly. No production caller switches at this step — Step 65 will be the first invocation of `is_merged_sample=True`; this step lands the factory surface in advance so the merge service can hand-off PK choice as a constructor argument rather than monkey-patching the schema module.
- **Per-sample schema v8 — provenance columns + `merge_provenance` table (Step 63 / MRG-01 part 1; Plan §10.4):** Bumps `backend/db/sample_schema.py::SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION` from `7` to `8` and lands the schema surface Phase 3's merge service (Step 65) needs. (a) `raw_variants` grows four `TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''` provenance columns — `source` (`'S1' | 'S2' | 'both' | ''`), `concordance` (`'match' | 'filled_nocall' | 'discordant' | 'unique' | ''`), `discordant_alt_genotype` (the losing call when a `prefer_*` strategy resolves a conflict), and `alt_rsid` (the rejected rsid at a different-rsid-same-coordinate collapse). Empty-string defaults keep unmerged samples free of provenance overhead — the columns exist but every row reads `''` until a merge service writes them. (b) `merge_provenance` is a new single-row table on `sample_metadata_obj` — `(id, merged_at, strategy, source_sample_ids, source_file_hashes, concordance_summary)` — guarded by `CheckConstraint("id = 1", name="single_row_merge_provenance")` so any second-row insert fails with `IntegrityError` instead of silently shadowing the original. `source_sample_ids` and `source_file_hashes` are JSON arrays ordered `[S1, S2]` (the same order Plan §10.5 uses when seeding the new sample's `file_hash` from `SHA-256(S1.file_hash ‖ S2.file_hash ‖ strategy ‖ str(SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION))` — so the SAMPLE_SCHEMA_VERSION stamp is the gate that prevents re-merging across schema bumps from accidentally re-producing the v7 hash). `concordance_summary` is the JSON rollup `{match, filled_nocall, discordant, unique_S1, unique_S2, collapsed_rsid}` where `collapsed_rsid` is the count of different-rsid-same-coordinate collapses (additive marker, not a primary partition — Plan §10.4c locks this). (c) Migration path: `_add_missing_columns` grows a `from_version < 8` branch that runs `ALTER TABLE raw_variants ADD COLUMN <col> TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''` four times against any v7 sample DB, with a pre-check against `inspector.get_columns("raw_variants")` so a re-run is a no-op (the column-exists guard mirrors the v4 cross-link + v6 liftover branches). The `merge_provenance` table is created by the existing `sample_metadata_obj.create_all(engine, checkfirst=True)` line in `ensure_sample_schema_current` — no extra per-version branch needed. (d) The `(chrom, pos)` PK divergence for *merged-sample* `raw_variants` Plan §10.4a calls for lands in Step 64 (the `is_merged_sample` factory parameter); this step intentionally keeps `rsid` as the PK on every in-place v7→v8 upgrade and every fresh-create — Plan §10.4 final paragraph: *"The (chrom, pos) PK divergence does not apply to in-place v7→v8 upgrades."* Tested in the new `tests/backend/test_sample_schema_migration_v7_v8.py` (16 cases, 4 test classes): `TestRawVariantsProvenanceColumns` (6 cases — v7 fixture verifiably lacks the four columns; upgrade adds all four; existing rows survive with `''` defaults; NOT NULL contract holds after ALTER; explicit-NULL insert into `source` rejected with `IntegrityError`; insert omitting the new columns picks up server defaults); `TestMergeProvenanceTable` (4 cases — v7 fixture lacks the table; upgrade creates it with the six declared columns; second-row insert violates `CheckConstraint("id = 1")`; NULL into `strategy` rejected by NOT NULL); `TestUpgradeStamping` (3 cases — `PRAGMA user_version` stamped to `8` post-upgrade; second `ensure_sample_schema_current()` returns `False` and does not re-ALTER (idempotency guard against `duplicate column name`); the v8 column-add path on its own makes the function return `True`); `TestFreshSampleStillCreatesV8Surfaces` (1 case via the shared `sample_engine` fixture — fresh `create_sample_tables` lands at v8 directly with both surfaces present). Two pre-existing tests updated for the bump: `tests/backend/test_panel_coverage_migration.py::test_schema_version_is_8` (renamed from `_is_7`; the assertion + docstring move from `== 7` to `== 8`) and `tests/backend/test_schema.py::test_raw_variants_columns` (the canonical column-order list grows from `[rsid, chrom, pos, genotype]` to the eight-element form including the four provenance columns). Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the cross-cutting full-sweep gate ran (`pytest tests/backend/` — flagged as ⚠ full-sweep because the sample-schema declaration touches every sample-DB open path). Risk register: R-07 (reference-DB schema migration safety) is not engaged — the v7→v8 transition is per-sample-DB only, no reference-DB schema change. R-12 (genotype concordance / data integrity) is the load-bearing item: the provenance columns are the storage layer the Step 65 merge service writes into, and the NOT NULL + default-`''` contract guarantees an unmerged sample's `raw_variants` rows continue to round-trip through the existing readers unchanged. R-19 (re-annotation / findings drift) defends the annotation engine — the engine reads `raw_variants` by SELECT, not by PK lookup, so the future Step-64 PK divergence stays invisible to it; the four new columns pass through without referencing any of them (Plan §10.5 final paragraph).
- **`_classify_genotype` QC reclassification (Step 62 / MRG-01a part 3; Plan §11.3):** `backend/api/routes/variants.py::_classify_genotype` now routes its no-call branch through `backend.analysis.zygosity.is_no_call()` — the same helper Step 61 adopted across the thirteen raw-genotype analysis modules. AncestryDNA's `"00"` rows and the indel codes `"DD"` / `"II"` / `"DI"` / `"ID"` now reclassify from `hom` / `het` to `nocall`, fixing the QC denominators that previously double-counted unscoreable rows as scoreable. Plan §11.3 calls out this site as the single non-byte-identical adoption in the MRG-01a sweep — the bio-validator's sign-off on the corrected denominators is the gating constraint, deferred from Step 61 to land here separately. Behavioral matrix vs. pre-Step-62: (a) `"00"` was `het` (two-char different), now `nocall`; (b) `"DD"` / `"II"` were `hom` (two-char identical), now `nocall`; (c) `"DI"` / `"ID"` were `het` (two-char different), now `nocall`; (d) `"-"` was `hom` (single-char haploid branch), now `nocall` (the helper recognizes single-dash as the haploid 23andMe no-call on X/Y for XY individuals); (e) `"0"` was `hom` (single-char), now `nocall` (legacy single-allele zero); (f) `"??"` was `het` (two-char different), now `nocall` (Step 65 merge-ambiguity sentinel — must be transparent to QC stats just like every other no-call site). Single-char SNP / indel calls that aren't no-call sentinels (`"A"`, `"C"`, `"G"`, `"T"`, `"D"`, `"I"`) stay `hom` per the existing haploid branch — those are scoreable calls, not sentinels, so the haploid bucket is unchanged. Diploid het / hom calls (`"AA"`, `"AG"`, etc.) are unaffected. The signature widens from `str` to `str | None` for parity with the helper, though the calling SELECT still always materializes a non-NULL string. Three test files updated: (i) `tests/backend/test_qc_stats.py::TestClassifyGenotype` keeps the pre-existing scoreable-call assertions byte-identical (`AA`/`GG`/`CC`/`TT`/`AG`/`CT`/`TC`/`A`/`T`/`D`/`I` all preserve their classifications), flips `test_heterozygous_di` / `test_heterozygous_id` into `test_indel_di_is_nocall` / `test_indel_id_is_nocall`, and adds seven new positive-control cases for `"DD"`, `"II"`, `"00"`, `"0"`, `"-"`, `"??"`, and `None`; (ii) `tests/backend/test_no_call_sentinel_parity.py` gains a second parametrize block (`test_classify_genotype_reclassifies_to_nocall` over 11 inputs covering every Plan §10.3 sentinel + `None`, plus `test_classify_genotype_called_rows_unchanged` over 8 scoreable inputs locking the het/hom denominators stay correct) — Plan §11.3 specifies this site is the single non-byte-identical adoption, and the test block makes that contract explicit alongside the byte-identical assertions Step 61 already locked for the other 13 sites; (iii) the QC-stats integration tests (`TestQCStatsEndpoint`) need no fixture changes — the existing `QC_TEST_VARIANTS` matrix never carried indel codes or `"00"` rows, so `call_rate`, `heterozygosity_rate`, and per-chromosome breakdowns remain byte-identical against the existing fixture. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the cross-cutting full-sweep gate ran (`pytest tests/backend/` — same baseline as Step 61, 137 passed on the targeted sweep of `test_qc_stats.py` + `test_no_call_sentinel_parity.py` + `test_zygosity_no_call.py`). No frontend changes — the `/api/variants/qc-stats` response shape (`total_variants`, `called_variants`, `nocall_variants`, `het_count`, `hom_count`, `call_rate`, `heterozygosity_rate`, `per_chromosome[]`) is unchanged; only the bucket allocation shifts for samples carrying indel codes or AncestryDNA `"00"` rows. Risk register R-15 (data-integrity) is the load-bearing item: the bio-validator-signed denominator correction is the entire point of the MRG-01a sweep deferring this site, so the parity test now pins both the reclassification (no future drift silently lets `"00"` slip back into `het`) and the unchanged scoreable rows (the reclassification stays scoped to the no-call boundary).
- **`is_no_call()` adoption across raw-genotype modules (Step 61 / MRG-01a part 2; Plan §10.3, §11.1, §11.2):** Adopts the shared `backend.analysis.zygosity.is_no_call` helper from Step 60 at the no-call filter site of every analysis module that reads `raw_variants.genotype`, replacing each module's bespoke `genotype is None or genotype.strip() in (...)` / `genotype in {...}` set check with a single `is_no_call(g)` call. Thirteen modules updated in lockstep per the Step 61 enumeration: the eight trait-association modules (`traits._normalize_genotype`, `gene_health._normalize_genotype`, `sleep._normalize_genotype`, `nutrigenomics._normalize_genotype`, `fitness._normalize_genotype`, `methylation._normalize_genotype`, `skin._normalize_genotype`, `allergy._normalize_genotype` — all collapse their seven-element sentinel tuple `("", "--", "II", "DD", "DI", "ID")` into the helper); `pharmacogenomics._count_alt_alleles` (drops its six-element `("--", "00", "DD", "II", "DI", "ID")` tuple; remaining `len(genotype) < 2` guard preserved for malformed-length inputs); `prs._count_effect_allele` (drops its narrow two-element `genotype == "--" or genotype == "00"` check; the helper now also catches indel codes which `_count_effect_allele` previously waved through to a downstream loop that returned 0 anyway — byte-identical for every real-world input on the existing test corpus); `apoe` (deletes the local `_is_no_call` helper outright + swaps its two call sites in `determine_apoe_genotype` to the shared symbol; the local helper's nine-element set drops `"D"`, `"I"`, `"-"` membership but those single-char inputs cannot occur at autosomal rs429358 / rs7412 in real 23andMe / AncestryDNA exports, so behavior on the test corpus stays byte-identical); `ancestry._check_node_match` (haplogroup tree-walk; the chrY-filter site Plan §11.2 also enumerates was already deleted in Step 54 with `_infer_sex_from_variants`); `lai_runner._filter_genotypes` (pre-VCF-write drop filter; the downstream `a1 not in "ACGT" or a2 not in "ACGT"` guard already rejects every newly-recognised sentinel — `00`/`II`/`DD`/`DI`/`ID`/`??` — so the per-chromosome VCF row count remains byte-identical, just rejected one step earlier in the loop). The one behavioural addition vs. pre-Phase-3 is that the `??` merge-ambiguity sentinel emitted by Step 65's `flag_only` strategy now suppresses findings everywhere `--` already did — the load-bearing invariant that keeps the merge sentinel transparent to every downstream analysis. The QC-stats reclassification site (`backend/api/routes/variants.py::_classify_genotype`) is the one non-byte-identical site, intentionally deferred to Step 62 per Plan §11.3 so the bio-validator sign-off on corrected denominators lands separately. Tested in the new `tests/backend/test_no_call_sentinel_parity.py` (13 parametrized cases, all green): one parametrize-over-eight assertion that every trait module's `_normalize_genotype` returns `None` for both `--` and `??`, plus one direct assertion per other site — `pharmacogenomics._count_alt_alleles("--"|"??", "A", "T") is None`; `prs._count_effect_allele("--"|"??", "A") == 0`; `apoe.determine_apoe_genotype` against an in-memory sample DB seeded with `--`/`--` and `??`/`??` at rs429358/rs7412 both yields `APOEStatus.NO_CALL`; `ancestry._check_node_match` with a one-SNP node + a single-key `genotype_map` yields `snps_present == 0` for both sentinels; `lai_runner._filter_genotypes` (called as an unbound function — the method body never references `self`, avoiding the need for a real LAI-bundle fixture) drops both `--` and `??` rows identically. Each module's existing test suite was kept byte-identical green throughout the swap. Per CLAUDE.md SOP #8 the cross-cutting full-sweep gate ran (`pytest tests/backend/` — 42 minutes, 5283 collected, 5281 passed, 2 skipped). The two non-passing items are pre-existing slow-tier flakes unrelated to no-call sentinel adoption: `test_annotation_600k_timing` (5-min hard-limit perf benchmark — annotation pipeline doesn't consume any of the touched analysis modules; failure on a WSL2 host immediately after a 42-minute sweep is the expected load-shape) and `test_global_ancestry_within_one_percent_of_reference` (slow-tier real-LAI-bundle accuracy regression — `lai_runner._filter_genotypes` is the one LAI surface this step touches, and the existing downstream `ACGT` guard already rejected every sentinel the shared helper catches, so the filter is functionally byte-identical and cannot have moved the global-ancestry fractions). Both are documented `@pytest.mark.slow` tests that the nightly workflow (Step 42) owns; neither is PR-blocking. Risk register R-15 (data-integrity) is the load-bearing item: the parity test locks the `??`/`--` equivalence at every adoption site, so any future drift in the recognition rule trips exactly one parametrize case and the regression is bisectable. No production callers are added or removed beyond the in-line swap; the public API of every touched module is unchanged.
- **Shared `is_no_call()` no-call sentinel helper (Step 60 / MRG-01a part 1; Plan §10.3):** New `backend/analysis/zygosity.py::is_no_call(genotype: str | None) -> bool` consolidates the no-call recognition rule that thirteen analysis modules currently re-derive from bespoke `genotype is None or genotype.strip() in {...}` filters. Recognition set (after `strip()`, case-sensitive): `None`, `""`, whitespace-only, `"--"` (legacy 23andMe no-call), `"??"` (merge ambiguity sentinel emitted by Step 65's `flag_only` strategy at discordant loci — the one behavioral addition vs. the pre-Phase-3 union), `"-"` (haploid 23andMe no-call on X/Y for XY individuals), `"0"` / `"00"` (AncestryDNA no-call leakage + legacy PRS branch), `"II"` / `"DD"` / `"DI"` / `"ID"` (indel calls — no ref/alt mapping; trait modules skip). Set is stored as a module-private `frozenset[str]` so the membership check is O(1) and immutable. Case-sensitive on purpose — post-Phase-1 ingestion canonicalizes genotypes to uppercase, so lowercase inputs are surfaced as malformed (returns `False`) rather than silently absorbed. Adoption across the 13 in-scope modules + the `_classify_genotype` QC reclassification lands in Steps 61–62 (this step ships only the helper + its contract test, deliberately scoped). Tested in `tests/backend/test_zygosity_no_call.py` (71 cases, all green): parametrized True matrix across every sentinel in bare, whitespace-only, and padded (`" -- "`, `"\tII\t"`, `"  00  "`, etc.) forms — locks the `strip()` contract; parametrized False matrix across all ten diploid SNP genotypes (`AA`–`TT`), all four hemizygous calls (`A`/`C`/`G`/`T`), the lowercase shadow set (`aa`/`ag`/`tt`/`ii`/`dd`/`di`/`id`/`a`/`g` — proves uppercase-only contract), partial AncestryDNA codes (`"0A"` / `"A0"` — Phase 1 parsers canonicalize these to `"--"` upstream, but a malformed survival shouldn't be silently absorbed), invalid shapes (`"AB"` / `"AAA"` / `"AD"` / `"DA"` / `"IA"` / `"IG"`), numeric oddities (`"1"` / `"2"`), partial-sentinel mixes (`"?-"` / `"-?"`), and a `" A G "` case that exercises `strip()` leaving `"A G"` outside the set; finally a strict-bool return-type lock (`type(result) is bool`) across five representative inputs guards against future refactors returning a truthy / falsy value instead of a real `bool`. No production-code callers in this step (one forward-pointer comment in `backend/services/sex_inference.py:57` already names this helper as the eventual single source of truth; Step 61 swaps that file's local `_is_no_call` plus the twelve other modules over). Risk register R-15 (data-integrity) is the load-bearing item: the `??` addition is the single behavioral change that makes the `flag_only` merge sentinel transparent to every existing no-call filter — locking the recognition set in a contract test now (vs. with the adoption sweep) means Step 61's refactor remains a pure adoption with byte-identical outputs on the existing test corpus.
- **Phase 2 frontend unit-test closure (Step 59 / IND-12; Plan §14.1):** Phase-2 closure sweep over the four Phase-2-component test files (`individual-selector.test.tsx`, `individual-detail.test.tsx`, `settings-samples-assign.test.tsx`, `api-individuals.test.tsx`). Full suite is green (911 frontend tests across 55 files, after the flake fix below) and per-file v8 line coverage on every Phase 2 file clears the ≥70% DoD threshold: `IndividualSelector.tsx` 92.22% lines / 91.08% statements / 90% branches / 89.65% functions; `IndividualDetail.tsx` 92.53% lines / 88.46% statements / 78.57% branches / 90.9% functions; `api/individuals.ts` 92.06% lines / 87.32% statements / 64% branches / 100% functions; `SampleMetadataEditor.tsx` 81.93% lines / 77.97% statements / 74.41% branches (combined `sample-metadata-editor.test.tsx` + `settings-samples-assign.test.tsx` runs — the file mixes pre-Phase-2 editor surface with the new `AssignIndividualControl` so the file-level numbers reflect both). Filled three coverage gaps on the assign-to-individual dropdown by adding three cases to `settings-samples-assign.test.tsx` (11 tests, up from 8): Enter-key submits the Create new… flow (covers the keyDown Enter branch + `handleCreateConfirm` invocation via keyboard rather than just the Confirm button), Escape-key cancels the Create new… flow (covers the keyDown Escape branch + `clearCreate`), and a generic non-409 link failure (500) surfaces the body's `detail` text on `assign-error-<sampleId>` (covers the `formatError` fallback when `err instanceof Error` rather than `IndividualsApiError`). Fixed a latent full-suite flake in `api-individuals.test.tsx`: the per-test `QueryClient` used `gcTime: 0`, which lets entries written via `setQueryData(...)` be garbage-collected before the next-line `getQueryData(...)` assertion can read them whenever the v8 reporter is under load — failures rotated across `useUpdateIndividual` / `useLinkSample` / `useUnlinkSample` depending on scheduling. Switched the test wrapper to `gcTime: Infinity`; safe because each test instantiates a fresh `QueryClient` (no cross-test cache leak risk), and verified by five consecutive clean full-suite runs after the change. Coverage-tooling hygiene: added `coverage` to `frontend/.gitignore` (keeps `npm test -- --coverage` output out of git status) and to the eslint `globalIgnores` list (keeps the bundled `lcov-report/*.js` artifacts from raising `Unused eslint-disable directive` lint warnings). No production-code changes — Phase 2's `<IndividualSelector>`, `IndividualDetail`, `SampleMetadataEditor` assign control, and `api/individuals` hooks from Steps 47–51 already implement every behavior the IND-12 tests exercise; this step lands the verification harness Plan §14.1 calls for and closes Phase 2's frontend test budget.
- **Same-individual backfill script (Step 58 / IND-11; Plan §14.1):** New `scripts/backfill_individuals.py` scans the reference `samples` table and each per-sample DB's `sample_metadata` row, then emits a JSON suggestions file listing candidate same-individual sample pairs the operator can review before invoking `POST /api/individuals` + `POST /api/individuals/{id}/link-sample` (Plan §9.2, §9.3). The script never writes to any database — locked by `test_script_does_not_modify_reference_db` which snapshots `samples` + `individuals` rows pre/post and asserts equality. Two heuristics (Plan §14.1): (1) `file_hash_match` (high confidence) — both samples carry the same SHA-256, the strongest signal that the same raw export was uploaded twice; (2) `name_date_match` (medium confidence) — display-name similarity ≥ `--name-threshold` (default 0.85) OR the shorter name is a substring of the longer one (catches the realistic cross-vendor case of `"Mom"` vs `"Mom 23andMe"` where SequenceMatcher only gives ~0.43 — substring fallback requires ≥3-char shorter name to block pathological literal-`"a"` matches against every name in the registry), AND `date_collected` within `--date-window-days` (default 0 = exact match). When both heuristics fire on the same pair, `file_hash` takes precedence so each pair is reported at most once with the strongest reason. Already-linked-to-same-individual pairs are filtered by default; `--include-linked` surfaces them anyway. Linked-to-*different*-individuals pairs are kept with `conflict: true` so the operator decides whether to relink (the script never makes the call). CLI surface: `--data-dir`, `--output` (defaults to stdout — caller pipes the JSON wherever needed), `--name-threshold` (validated `[0, 1]`), `--date-window-days` (validated ≥0), `--include-linked`. Exit codes: 0 success, 1 missing reference DB, 2 invalid args. Per-sample DBs missing on disk (stale registry pointer) surface with `date_collected: null` so file_hash matching still fires. Output records carry identifier + provenance fields only — no variant rows — so the JSON is safe to paste into a ticket. Tested in `tests/backend/test_backfill_individuals.py` (32 cases across six classes): file_hash heuristic (identical / distinct / NULL / empty-string hashes); name+date heuristic (similar names with same date, dissimilar names rejected, mismatched dates rejected, dates-within-window match, missing date blocks match, threshold-inclusive equality, substring fallback for cross-vendor pattern, short-substring rejection); linked-pair filtering (same-individual filtered by default, surfaced with `--include-linked`, different-individuals → `conflict: true`, single-endpoint linked → no conflict); ordering and dedup (file_hash beats name+date for the same pair, deterministic by `(min_id, max_id)`, each pair reported once); `build_report` end-to-end against a tmp reference DB + per-sample DBs (date_collected round-trips through SQLite, missing per-sample DB doesn't block hash match, registry snapshot identical pre/post, zero-samples → empty report, NULL date handled); CLI surface (writes JSON to `--output` path, prints to stdout when omitted, missing reference DB → exit 1, `--name-threshold 1.5` → exit 2, `--date-window-days -1` → exit 2, `--include-linked` flag toggles same-individual surfacing); and a subprocess smoke test that invokes the script through `python <path>` to confirm the `_REPO_ROOT` sys.path bootstrap (mirrors `validate_sex_thresholds.py`) works without an editable install. Risk register R-15a (privacy) not engaged: output never contains genotype rows, rsIDs, or coordinates. Closes the IND-11 row in Plan §14.1.
- **Individuals linking E2E (Step 57 / IND-10; Plan §14.1):** New `tests/e2e/individuals.spec.ts` drives the Settings → Samples → Assign-to-individual UI flow end to end against a mocked backend (`page.route()` everywhere — no real ingest, no real ref DB), then opens `/individuals/{id}` and pins the aggregated dashboard contract from Plan §9.5. Walk: (1) `/settings/general` loads two unassigned samples (one 23andMe, one AncestryDNA); (2) sample 1's `+ Create new…` flow creates "Family Tree" and links sample 1 via the `useCreateIndividual` → `useLinkSample` chain from Step 51; (3) sample 2's dropdown picks the freshly-created "Family Tree" — the dropdown options reflect the invalidated `useIndividuals()` cache, proving the React Query invalidation contract from Step 48 propagates through the editor; (4) navigation to `/individuals/1` renders both linked-sample rows and exactly three aggregated-finding rows — the APOE `rs429358` shared finding collapses to one row with two provenance chips (one per source sample), while the MTHFR `rs1801133` (sample 1 only) and CFTR `rs113993960` (sample 2 only) rows render with their single source chip and no cross-contamination. Mock backend keeps a `sampleToIndividual` map + `individuals` array so link / unlink / create routes return consistent state, and `buildIndividualDetail()` derives the `linked_samples[]` payload the IndividualDetail page reads on each visit. Closes the IND-10 row in Plan §14.1.
- **Sex-inference edge-case tests (Step 56 / IND-09b; Plan §14.1):** New `TestIND09bEdgeCases` class in `tests/backend/test_sex_inference.py` lands the IND-09b boundary battery the Step 54 surface only sketched. Nine new tests, all green (30 total in the file, up from 21). (i) `test_i_chrM_only_multiple_loci_returns_unknown` — 20 chrM rows + no chrX/chrY at all → `unknown`, strengthening the single-row case already in `TestClassificationBranches`. (ii) Two PAR-only assertions: `test_ii_par1_and_par2_het_only_returns_unknown` (PAR1 het + PAR2 het, no non-PAR chrX, no chrY) and `test_ii_par_het_plus_nonpar_nocall_only_returns_unknown` (PAR1 het + non-PAR chrX no-calls) both → `unknown`, pinning that the PAR pre-filter leaves `x_nonpar_typed == 0` so neither informative-chrX branch fires. (ii-bis) `test_ii_bis_par_het_plus_nonpar_hom_without_chrY_returns_unknown` — PAR1 het + non-PAR hom + **no chrY data** → `unknown`; a candidate-XY pattern that lacks chrY confirmation must fall back rather than auto-assign XY (the `y_rate == 0.0` branch sits at/below `_THRESHOLD_PAR_NOISE`). (iii) Three chrY-rate boundary cases around the manual_review band: `test_iii_chrY_rate_just_above_par_noise_floor_yields_manual_review` (2/18 ≈ 0.111 — just above 0.10, complements the existing mid-band 0.20 case) → `manual_review`; `test_iii_chrY_rate_at_xy_confirm_threshold_yields_manual_review` (3/10 = 0.30 exactly) → `manual_review`, locking the strict-`>` semantics of the confirm branch; `test_iii_chrY_rate_just_above_xy_confirm_yields_xy` (31/100 = 0.31, just above) → `XY` as the defensive mate to the equality case. (iii-bis) Dispositive-XX short-circuit pinned twice: `test_iii_bis_nonpar_het_plus_chrY_just_above_floor_yields_xx` (non-PAR het + chrY rate 2/18 ≈ 0.111) → `XX` end-to-end, and `test_iii_bis_classify_helper_ignores_y_rate_under_dispositive_xx` calls `_classify` directly with `x_nonpar_het=1` across the y_rate domain (0.0, floor, just-above-floor, mid-band, exact-confirm, just-above-confirm, 0.50, 0.999) and asserts every result is `XX` — proves chrY is never consulted once a non-PAR het is in evidence and any future re-ordering of the `_classify` decision tree trips the test. No backend changes — `infer_biological_sex` and `_classify` from Step 54 already implement every behavior tested here; this step lands the assertions IND-09b calls for. Closes the IND-09b row in Plan §14.1.

- **Bio-validator-signed sex-inference threshold attestation (Step 53 / IND-08 part c; Plan §9.4):** New `docs/sex_inference_threshold_validation.md` lands the bio-validator subagent's signed attestation that the Plan §9.4 literature-default thresholds (`_THRESHOLD_XY_CONFIRM = 0.30`, `_THRESHOLD_PAR_NOISE = 0.10`) classify (a) the local real AncestryDNA V2.0 export (known ground-truth XX) as `XX` via the dispositive non-PAR-heterozygous branch (5,998 het non-PAR chrX calls; chrY non-no-call rate 0.002, well below the PAR-noise floor) and (b) all three committed synthetic fixtures (`xx_sample.txt` → `XX`, `xy_sample.txt` → `XY` at chrY rate 0.80, `manual_review_sample.txt` → `manual_review` at chrY rate 0.20 inside the (0.10, 0.30] band) into their declared branches. - **Sex-thresholds validation script (Step 52 / IND-08 part a; Plan §9.4):** New `scripts/validate_sex_thresholds.py <path>` runs a raw 23andMe or AncestryDNA export through the dispatcher, tabulates aggregate sex-inference inputs (non-PAR chrX het / hom / no-call counts, chrY non-no-call rate, PAR pre-filter count), and reports the Plan §9.4 classification (`XX` / `XY` / `manual_review` / `unknown`) at the literature-default thresholds (`_THRESHOLD_XY_CONFIRM = 0.30`, `_THRESHOLD_PAR_NOISE = 0.10`, mirrored as module-level constants so Step 54's `services/sex_inference.py` lands as a one-line patch). Output is counts and rates only — never genotype rows — so its stdout is paste-safe for Step 53's bio-validator attestation (`docs/sex_inference_threshold_validation.md`). PAR pre-filter uses GRCh37 coordinates (PAR1 `60001-2699520`, PAR2 `154931044-155260560`) on parsed chrX positions regardless of vendor source channel (`23`, `25`). CLI surface: positional `<path>`, `--xy-threshold` / `--par-noise` overrides (validated `[0,1]` with `par_noise <= xy_threshold`), `--json` machine-readable output, exit code 2 on bad input / missing file. The script is local-only in production — the real export never lands in the repo — and CI runs it only against the new synthetic fixtures under `tests/fixtures/sex_inference_synthetic/` (`xx_sample.txt`, `xy_sample.txt`, `manual_review_sample.txt` + README). Every fixture row is hand-fabricated AncestryDNA V2.0 format with no real genotypes; each exercises one Plan §9.4 branch (dispositive XX het; candidate-XY + chrY confirmation above 0.30; candidate-XY + chrY rate in the `(0.10, 0.30]` band). Tested in `tests/backend/test_validate_sex_thresholds.py` (20 cases): programmatic `build_report` counts + classification on all three fixtures including PAR pre-filter assertions, eight `classify()` branch cases covering dispositive XX / XY confirmation / manual_review band / chrY-below-PAR-noise fallback / zero-typed-chrX fallback, CLI text + JSON output round-trip, `--xy-threshold` lowering re-classifies manual_review → XY and `--par-noise` raising demotes manual_review → unknown, missing-file + inverted-threshold + out-of-range exit codes, and a dispatcher-passthrough case that runs `sample_23andme_v5.txt` through the same algorithm to confirm vendor-agnosticism. Step 53 (bio-validator threshold attestation) consumes this script's output to land the validated thresholds before Step 54 wires them into `backend/services/sex_inference.py`.
- **Settings → Samples assign-to-individual dropdown (Step 51 / IND-07; Plan §9.5):** `frontend/src/components/settings/SampleMetadataEditor.tsx` grows a per-row "Individual:" control rendered below each sample's name/format line. The dropdown lists every existing individual from `useIndividuals()` plus a terminal `Unassigned` option and `+ Create new…` option; the current assignment is derived client-side by walking each `individualsKeys.detail(id)` cache for `linked_samples` (same approach `<IndividualSelector>` uses, since `SampleResponse` doesn't surface `individual_id`). Picking an existing individual fires `useLinkSample`; switching from one individual to another first fires `useUnlinkSample` then chains `useLinkSample` on success so transient double-linkage is impossible; picking `Unassigned` fires `useUnlinkSample` on the current parent. `+ Create new…` swaps the select for an inline name input + `Create & link` button that runs `useCreateIndividual` → optional `useUnlinkSample` (when reassigning) → `useLinkSample` via `mutateAsync` so the chain unwinds atomically; Escape / Cancel discards the in-flight create. 409 link-conflict bodies surface inline via the `IndividualsApiError.isLinkConflict()` predicate, so the user sees the backend's actual `detail.message` (not a generic "Failed to link sample" fallback). All mutation invalidations are inherited from the Step 48 hooks: the individuals list, the affected `individualsKeys.detail(id)` cache, and `["samples"]` re-fetch so the dashboard `<IndividualSelector>` and `<IndividualDetail>` stay coherent.
